Sects and Disagreements

The Hadith of the 73 Sects
The author cites the hadith of 73 sects from al-Tirmidhi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic hadith about the 73 sects and that the saved sect is the one following the Prophet and his Companions.

Core Idea
The saved sect is the one that follows the Prophet and his Companions.

The Prophet ﷺ informed us that his nation would split into 73 sects, all destined for the Fire except one. This lesson presents the authentic hadith and clarifies that the saved sect is the one that adheres to the path of the Prophet and his Companions, not any particular group or party.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the precise wording: 'what I and my Companions are upon.'
This is a direct and clear criterion for salvation.
2
Identify the saved sect
The hadith explicitly states that the saved sect is the one following the Prophet and his Companions. Reflect on what this means: the true path is the original Islam as practiced by the first generation.
3
Consider the significance
Why is this hadith important? It warns against division and provides a clear standard for evaluating beliefs and practices.
This hadith is foundational for Sunni orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما أخبر به الصادق وفق الواقع المطابق وغيره على ما رواه الترمذي أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: ((إن بني إسرائيل تفرقت على ثنتين وسبعين ملة، وتفرق أمتي على ثلاث وسبعين ملة، كلهم في النار إلا ملة واحدة، قالوا: من هي يارسول الله؟ قال: ما أنا عليه وأصحابي)).(۱) وفي رواية أحمد وأبي داود عن معاوية رضي الله عنه: «ثنتان وسبعون في النار وواحدة في الجنة وهي الجماعة».(٢) يعني أكثر أهل الملة، فإن أمته عليه الصلوة والسلام لا تجتمع على الضلالة على ما ورد عنه عليه الصلوة والسلام، وفي رواية: (عليكم بالسواد الأعظم).(۳) وعن سفيان رضي الله عنه: «لو أن فقيها واحدا على رأس جبل لكان هو الجماعة». ومعناه أنه حيث قام بما قام به الجماعة فكأنه جماعة. ومنه قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ إِبْرَاهِيمَ كَانَ أُمَّةً ﴾ [النحل:١٢٠] أي وحده. وقد قيل: وليس على الله بمستنكر أن يجمع العالم في واحد. وقد قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنه: «تكفل الله لمن قرأ القرآن وعمل بما فيه بأن لا يضل في الدنيا ولا يشقى في العقبى، ثم قرأ هذه الآية: ﴿ فَمَنِ اتَّبَعَ هُدَايَ فَلَا يَضِلُّ وَلَا يَشْقَى [طه: ۱۲۳] .»
As reported by the truthful one, in accordance with actual reality and others, according to what al-Tirmidhi narrated that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Indeed, the Children of Israel split into seventy-two sects, and my nation will split into seventy-three sects. All of them are in the Fire except one sect.' They said: 'Who is it, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'That which I and my Companions are upon.' (1) And in a narration by Ahmad and Abu Dawud from Mu'awiyah, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Seventy-two in the Fire and one in Paradise, and that is the Jama'ah (the main body).' (2) Meaning the majority of the nation, for his nation ﷺ does not unite upon error, as reported from him ﷺ. And in a narration: 'You must adhere to the largest mass (al-sawad al-a'zam).' (3) And from Sufyan, may Allah be pleased with him: 'If there is a single jurist on top of a mountain, he is the Jama'ah.' Its meaning is that when he stands for what the Jama'ah stands for, he is as if he is the Jama'ah. From this is the saying of Allah Most High: 'Indeed, Abraham was a nation' [Quran 16:120], i.e., alone. And it has been said: And it is not impossible for Allah to gather the world in one. And Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'Allah has guaranteed for whoever recites the Quran and acts according to what is in it that he will not go astray in this world nor be miserable in the Hereafter. Then he recited this verse: "Whoever follows My guidance will not go astray nor be miserable" [Quran 20:123].'
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage presents the prophetic hadith about the 73 sects. The author cites the hadith to show that the saved sect is the one following the Prophet and his Companions. He then explains that the 'jama'ah' (majority) is the saved group, meaning the majority of the Muslim community, because the Prophet guaranteed that his community would not unite on error. He adds the narration about the 'sawad al-a'zam' (large mass) and Sufyan's interpretation that even a single scholar following the truth is considered the jama'ah. He illustrates this with the Quranic verse about Abraham being a nation alone. Finally, he quotes Ibn Abbas to emphasize the guarantee of guidance for those who follow the Quran. This whole argument reinforces the importance of adhering to the inherited Islamic tradition as the path to salvation.

Key Terms
الفرقة الناجية
ملة
الصادق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the saved sect refers to a specific historical group like the Ash'aris or Maturidis.
Correction: The hadith does not name a specific group; it defines the saved sect as those who follow the Prophet and his Companions, which is a path of orthodoxy based on the Salaf.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi, what is the saved sect?
A) The group that has the most members.
B) The group that follows what the Prophet and his Companions were upon.
C) The group that uses reason over revelation.
D) The group that avoids all theological debates.

Key Takeaway
The saved sect is the one that follows the Prophet Muhammad and his Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear 'the saved sect,' does your mind immediately jump to the label you associate with yourself? How does the Prophet's answer—'what I and my Companions are upon'—challenge your assumption that your own group is automatically included?
?
The Prophet said all sects except one are in the Fire. Does this warning unsettle you? What would it look like for you to personally ensure you are on that saved path, regardless of what others around you do?
?
The saved path is defined by following what the Prophet and his Companions were upon. Are there any practices or beliefs you hold that you have never examined against this standard? Will you commit to studying the way of the Companions and comparing it to your own life?

The Meaning of al-Jama'ah and the Guarantee of Guidance
The author explains the saved sect as al-Jama'ah and cites additional hadith and quotes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the saved sect (al-Jama'ah) refers to the majority of the Muslim community and that even a single scholar upholding the truth is considered part of it, and that Allah guarantees guidance for those who follow the Quran.

Core Idea
The saved sect is the main body (Jama'ah) which can be represented by a single true scholar.

Building on the hadith of the 73 sects, the author further explains that the saved sect is called al-Jama'ah, meaning the majority of the nation. He cites additional narrations about adhering to the largest mass (al-sawad al-a'zam) and the interpretation of Sufyan that even one true jurist on a mountain can be the Jama'ah. This lesson clarifies the concept of communal orthodoxy and emphasizes the Quranic guarantee of guidance for those who follow divine guidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of Jama'ah
The author explains that 'jama'ah' means the majority of the nation, and that the Prophet's nation does not unite on error. Read the supporting narrations from Ahmad and Abu Dawud.
This reinforces the idea of communal consensus as a source of truth.
2
Understand the concept of 'sawad al-a'zam'
The narration 'You must adhere to the largest mass' connects the saved sect to the main body of Muslims throughout history.
3
Consider the single scholar example
Sufyan's statement shows that even one scholar standing for the truth can represent the whole Jama'ah. Reflect on the Quranic example of Abraham being a nation alone.
This highlights that truth is not solely determined by numbers.
4
Realize the divine guarantee
Ibn Abbas's quote ties following the Quran to guidance and salvation, completing the passage's emphasis on adhering to divine revelation.
This is a strong spiritual incentive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما أخبر به الصادق وفق الواقع المطابق وغيره على ما رواه الترمذي أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: ((إن بني إسرائيل تفرقت على ثنتين وسبعين ملة، وتفرق أمتي على ثلاث وسبعين ملة، كلهم في النار إلا ملة واحدة، قالوا: من هي يارسول الله؟ قال: ما أنا عليه وأصحابي)).(۱) وفي رواية أحمد وأبي داود عن معاوية رضي الله عنه: «ثنتان وسبعون في النار وواحدة في الجنة وهي الجماعة».(٢) يعني أكثر أهل الملة، فإن أمته عليه الصلوة والسلام لا تجتمع على الضلالة على ما ورد عنه عليه الصلوة والسلام، وفي رواية: (عليكم بالسواد الأعظم).(۳) وعن سفيان رضي الله عنه: «لو أن فقيها واحدا على رأس جبل لكان هو الجماعة». ومعناه أنه حيث قام بما قام به الجماعة فكأنه جماعة. ومنه قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ إِبْرَاهِيمَ كَانَ أُمَّةً ﴾ [النحل:١٢٠] أي وحده. وقد قيل: وليس على الله بمستنكر أن يجمع العالم في واحد. وقد قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنه: «تكفل الله لمن قرأ القرآن وعمل بما فيه بأن لا يضل في الدنيا ولا يشقى في العقبى، ثم قرأ هذه الآية: ﴿ فَمَنِ اتَّبَعَ هُدَايَ فَلَا يَضِلُّ وَلَا يَشْقَى [طه: ۱۲۳] .»
As reported by the truthful one, in accordance with actual reality and others, according to what al-Tirmidhi narrated that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Indeed, the Children of Israel split into seventy-two sects, and my nation will split into seventy-three sects. All of them are in the Fire except one sect.' They said: 'Who is it, O Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'That which I and my Companions are upon.' (1) And in a narration by Ahmad and Abu Dawud from Mu'awiyah, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Seventy-two in the Fire and one in Paradise, and that is the Jama'ah (the main body).' (2) Meaning the majority of the nation, for his nation ﷺ does not unite upon error, as reported from him ﷺ. And in a narration: 'You must adhere to the largest mass (al-sawad al-a'zam).' (3) And from Sufyan, may Allah be pleased with him: 'If there is a single jurist on top of a mountain, he is the Jama'ah.' Its meaning is that when he stands for what the Jama'ah stands for, he is as if he is the Jama'ah. From this is the saying of Allah Most High: 'Indeed, Abraham was a nation' [Quran 16:120], i.e., alone. And it has been said: And it is not impossible for Allah to gather the world in one. And Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'Allah has guaranteed for whoever recites the Quran and acts according to what is in it that he will not go astray in this world nor be miserable in the Hereafter. Then he recited this verse: "Whoever follows My guidance will not go astray nor be miserable" [Quran 20:123].'

Commentary
This passage presents the prophetic hadith about the 73 sects. The author cites the hadith to show that the saved sect is the one following the Prophet and his Companions. He then explains that the 'jama'ah' (majority) is the saved group, meaning the majority of the Muslim community, because the Prophet guaranteed that his community would not unite on error. He adds the narration about the 'sawad al-a'zam' (large mass) and Sufyan's interpretation that even a single scholar following the truth is considered the jama'ah. He illustrates this with the Quranic verse about Abraham being a nation alone. Finally, he quotes Ibn Abbas to emphasize the guarantee of guidance for those who follow the Quran. This whole argument reinforces the importance of adhering to the inherited Islamic tradition as the path to salvation.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does 'al-Jama'ah' refer to in the hadith?
A) A specific school of thought.
B) The majority of the Muslim nation.
C) The group of scholars only.
D) The Prophet's family.

Key Takeaway
The saved sect is the Jama'ah, the main body of Muslims adhering to the truth, which can even be represented by a single true scholar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where the majority around you seems to be following something contrary to the truth, do you have the courage to stand alone like Abraham, trusting that Allah’s guidance is sufficient? What would it cost you to be that 'single jurist on a mountaintop'?
?
If you truly believed that following the Quran guarantees you will not go astray in this world nor be miserable in the next, would your relationship with the Quran look different today? What is one concrete change you need to make to prioritize it?
?
Are you more concerned about being on the 'winning side' numerically or about being on the side of truth, even if it means being alone? Examine your heart: do you seek validation from the crowd more than from Allah?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
5 min
Abu Yusuf's Condemnation of Kalam
Abu Yusuf's statements condemning kalam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Abu Yusuf's paradoxical statement about kalam and the intended meanings behind it.

Core Idea
True knowledge is ignorance of false kalam.

Abu Yusuf's statement to Bishr al-Marisi is often quoted to condemn all theological discussion. But the author clarifies that Abu Yusuf did not advocate literal ignorance; rather, he meant that believing kalam to be false is itself beneficial knowledge, or that turning away from it preserves one's intellect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the direct quote from Abu Yusuf and the two interpretations given by the author.
The phrase 'knowledge of kalam is ignorance' is deliberately provocative.
2
Understand the paradox
Why would calling something 'ignorance' be considered a form of knowledge? Explore the two explanations: believing kalam is false, or ignoring it entirely.
3
Analyze the second quote
Read Abu Yusuf's additional warning: seeking kalam leads to heresy. Compare with seeking wealth through alchemy or strange hadith.
This reinforces the danger of kalam.
4
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Consider how this passage shaped early Islamic attitudes toward speculative theology.
This condemnation was a major factor in the development of traditionalist vs rationalist schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما وقع من كراهة أكثر السلف وجمع من الخلف ومنعهم من علم الكلام وما يتبعه من المنطق وما يقربه من المرام حتى قال الإمام أبو يوسف رحمه الله لبشر المريسي: «العلم بالكلام هو الجهل والجهل بالكلام هو العلم». وكأنه أراد بالجهل به اعتقاد عدم صحته، فإن ذلك علم نافع، أو أراد به الإعراض عنه وترك الإلتفات إلى اعتباره، فإن ذلك يصون علم الرجل وعقله فيكون علما بهذا الاعتبار. وعنه أيضاً : من طلب العلم بالكلام تزندق ومن طلب المال بالكيمياء أفلس ومن طلب غريب الحديث فقد كذب». وقال الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله: «حكمي أهل الكلام أن يضربوا بالجريد والنعال ويطاف بهم في العشائر والقبائل ويقال هذا جزاء من ترك الكتاب والسنة وأقبل على كلام أهل البدعة». وقال أيضاً: كل العلوم سوى القرآن مشغلة إلا الحديث وإلا الفقه في الدين العلم ما كان فيه "قال حدثنا" وما سوى ذلك وسواس الشياطين كلامه أيضاً: «لأن يلقى الله العبد بكل ذنب خلا الشرك خير له من أن يلقاه بشيء من علم الكلام». وقال: «لقد اطلعت من أهل الكلام على شيء ما ظننت مسلماً يقوله». وذكر أصحابنا في الفتاوى «أنه لو أوصى لعلماء بلده لا يدخل المتكلمون ولو أوصى إنسان كتب العلم فأفتى السلف أنه يباع ما فيها من كتب الكلام». ذكر ذلك بمعناه في الفتاوى الظهيرية وهو كلام مستحسن عند أرباب العقول إذ كيف يرام الوصول إلى علم الأصول بغير اتباع ما جاء به الرسول. والله دَرّ القائل في هذا المقول: أيها المغتدي لتطلب علما كل علم عبد لعلم الرسول تطلب العلم كي تصحح أصلا كيف أغفلت علم أصل الأصول
And as for what occurred of dislike by most of the Salaf and a group of the Khalaf and their prohibition of the science of kalam and what follows it of logic and what brings near it, even to the point that Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said to Bishr al-Marisi: 'Knowledge of kalam is ignorance, and ignorance of kalam is knowledge.' And it is as if he meant by ignorance of it the belief in its incorrectness, for that is beneficial knowledge. Or he meant by it turning away from it and not paying attention to considering it, for that preserves a man's knowledge and intellect, and thus it becomes knowledge in this respect. And from him also: 'Whoever seeks knowledge of kalam becomes a heretic; whoever seeks wealth through alchemy becomes bankrupt; and whoever seeks strange hadith becomes a liar.' And Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'My ruling regarding the people of kalam is that they should be beaten with palm stalks and sandals, and paraded among the tribes and clans, and it should be said: This is the punishment of one who abandoned the Book and the Sunnah and turned to the speech of the people of innovation.' And he also said: 'Every science besides the Quran is a distraction except hadith and the understanding of religion; knowledge is what contains "he said, we were narrated", and other than that is the whisperings of devils.' And also his statement: 'For a servant to meet Allah with every sin except shirk is better for him than to meet Him with any part of the knowledge of kalam.' And he said: 'I have seen from the people of kalam something that I never thought a Muslim would say.' And our companions mentioned in the fatwa: 'If someone bequeathed to the scholars of his town, the speculative theologians (mutakallimun) are not included; and if a person bequeaths books of knowledge, the Salaf gave a fatwa that books of kalam should be sold.' The author mentioned this in the al-Zuhayriyya fatwa, and it is commendable speech according to people of intellect, for how can one hope to reach the science of fundamental principles (usul) without following what the Messenger brought? And well said the one who recited: 'O you who go out seeking knowledge, every knowledge is a servant to the knowledge of the Messenger. You seek knowledge to correct a principle; how have you neglected the knowledge of the principle of principles?'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage presents a series of severe condemnations of kalam (dialectical theology) by early authorities. It begins by stating that most Salaf and some Khalaf disliked and prohibited kalam, logic, and related sciences. The first quote is from Abu Yusuf to Bishr al-Marisi: 'Knowledge of kalam is ignorance, and ignorance of kalam is knowledge.' The author explains that this means either believing kalam to be false is beneficial, or ignoring it preserves one's intellect. Abu Yusuf also says that seeking kalam leads to heresy (tazannuq). Next, al-Shafi'i's harsh ruling is cited: people of kalam should be beaten and paraded as a punishment for abandoning the Quran and Sunnah. Al-Shafi'i also says that only hadith and fiqh are true knowledge, and that meeting Allah with any sin except shirk is better than meeting Him with any kalam. He adds that he witnessed heretical statements from people of kalam. Then a fatwa from the author's school is mentioned: bequests for scholars exclude mutakallimun, and books of kalam should be sold. The author endorses this fatwa, arguing that one cannot reach the science of usul (principles) without following the Prophet. The passage concludes with a poem stating that all knowledge is subordinate to the knowledge of the Prophet.

Key Terms
كلام
جهل
تزندق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Abu Yusuf literally meant that ignorance of all kalam is knowledge and that studying kalam is always forbidden.
Correction: Abu Yusuf meant that believing kalam to be false is beneficial knowledge, or that ignoring it preserves one's religion and intellect. He did not prohibit all theological inquiry but condemned the kalam of innovators.

Checkpoint
According to the author, which of the following is one of the two interpretations of Abu Yusuf's statement 'ignorance of kalam is knowledge'?
A) That one should never speak about theological topics
B) That ignoring kalam preserves a man's intellect and becomes knowledge
C) That ignorance is always better than knowledge
D) That kalam is the same as logic

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf condemned kalam as leading to heresy, but his paradoxical statement is meant to highlight the danger, not to forbid all theological reflection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Yusuf says knowledge of kalam is ignorance. What 'knowledge' in your own life—whether of worldly matters or religious debates—might actually be ignorance of the truth? Are there topics you discuss that distance you from Allah rather than bring you closer? What one step can you take this week to turn away from such talk?
?
The Salaf turned away from kalam to preserve their intellect. What distractions or arguments do you need to actively ignore to preserve your own faith and mental clarity? How can you discipline yourself to avoid engaging in useless theological disputes?
?
If seeking knowledge of kalam can lead to heresy (tazanduq), what does that reveal about the spiritual danger of debating religion without pure intention? Do you ever argue about Islam to prove yourself right or to impress others? How can you repent from that and seek knowledge with humility?

Sects and Disagreements

Al-Shafi'i's Severe Condemnation of Kalam
Al-Shafi'i's condemnations of kalam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the forceful disapproval of kalam by Imam al-Shafi'i and the reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
For al-Shafi'i, kalam is worse than major sins except shirk.

Imam al-Shafi'i's statements against the people of kalam are among the harshest recorded. He prescribed physical punishment and declared that meeting Allah with any sin except shirk is better than engaging in kalam. This lesson examines his words and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Shafi'i's ruling and statements
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the physical punishment he prescribed and his strong words about kalam being worse than sins.
His ruling involves beating and parading the offenders.
2
Understand the context of his condemnation
Al-Shafi'i considered kalam a distraction from the Quran and Sunnah. He emphasized that true knowledge is only in hadith and fiqh.
3
Reflect on the extreme comparison
Al-Shafi'i said encountering Allah with any sin (except shirk) is better than with any part of kalam. This underscores his view of kalam's danger.
This is a very strong statement.
4
Connect to broader lesson
Consider how this shaped the traditionalist opposition to kalam.
Such statements were influential in rejecting speculative theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما وقع من كراهة أكثر السلف وجمع من الخلف ومنعهم من علم الكلام وما يتبعه من المنطق وما يقربه من المرام حتى قال الإمام أبو يوسف رحمه الله لبشر المريسي: «العلم بالكلام هو الجهل والجهل بالكلام هو العلم». وكأنه أراد بالجهل به اعتقاد عدم صحته، فإن ذلك علم نافع، أو أراد به الإعراض عنه وترك الإلتفات إلى اعتباره، فإن ذلك يصون علم الرجل وعقله فيكون علما بهذا الاعتبار. وعنه أيضاً : من طلب العلم بالكلام تزندق ومن طلب المال بالكيمياء أفلس ومن طلب غريب الحديث فقد كذب». وقال الإمام الشافعي رحمه الله: «حكمي أهل الكلام أن يضربوا بالجريد والنعال ويطاف بهم في العشائر والقبائل ويقال هذا جزاء من ترك الكتاب والسنة وأقبل على كلام أهل البدعة». وقال أيضاً: كل العلوم سوى القرآن مشغلة إلا الحديث وإلا الفقه في الدين العلم ما كان فيه "قال حدثنا" وما سوى ذلك وسواس الشياطين كلامه أيضاً: «لأن يلقى الله العبد بكل ذنب خلا الشرك خير له من أن يلقاه بشيء من علم الكلام». وقال: «لقد اطلعت من أهل الكلام على شيء ما ظننت مسلماً يقوله». وذكر أصحابنا في الفتاوى «أنه لو أوصى لعلماء بلده لا يدخل المتكلمون ولو أوصى إنسان كتب العلم فأفتى السلف أنه يباع ما فيها من كتب الكلام». ذكر ذلك بمعناه في الفتاوى الظهيرية وهو كلام مستحسن عند أرباب العقول إذ كيف يرام الوصول إلى علم الأصول بغير اتباع ما جاء به الرسول. والله دَرّ القائل في هذا المقول: أيها المغتدي لتطلب علما كل علم عبد لعلم الرسول تطلب العلم كي تصحح أصلا كيف أغفلت علم أصل الأصول
And as for what occurred of dislike by most of the Salaf and a group of the Khalaf and their prohibition of the science of kalam and what follows it of logic and what brings near it, even to the point that Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said to Bishr al-Marisi: 'Knowledge of kalam is ignorance, and ignorance of kalam is knowledge.' And it is as if he meant by ignorance of it the belief in its incorrectness, for that is beneficial knowledge. Or he meant by it turning away from it and not paying attention to considering it, for that preserves a man's knowledge and intellect, and thus it becomes knowledge in this respect. And from him also: 'Whoever seeks knowledge of kalam becomes a heretic; whoever seeks wealth through alchemy becomes bankrupt; and whoever seeks strange hadith becomes a liar.' And Imam al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'My ruling regarding the people of kalam is that they should be beaten with palm stalks and sandals, and paraded among the tribes and clans, and it should be said: This is the punishment of one who abandoned the Book and the Sunnah and turned to the speech of the people of innovation.' And he also said: 'Every science besides the Quran is a distraction except hadith and the understanding of religion; knowledge is what contains "he said, we were narrated", and other than that is the whisperings of devils.' And also his statement: 'For a servant to meet Allah with every sin except shirk is better for him than to meet Him with any part of the knowledge of kalam.' And he said: 'I have seen from the people of kalam something that I never thought a Muslim would say.' And our companions mentioned in the fatwa: 'If someone bequeathed to the scholars of his town, the speculative theologians (mutakallimun) are not included; and if a person bequeaths books of knowledge, the Salaf gave a fatwa that books of kalam should be sold.' The author mentioned this in the al-Zuhayriyya fatwa, and it is commendable speech according to people of intellect, for how can one hope to reach the science of fundamental principles (usul) without following what the Messenger brought? And well said the one who recited: 'O you who go out seeking knowledge, every knowledge is a servant to the knowledge of the Messenger. You seek knowledge to correct a principle; how have you neglected the knowledge of the principle of principles?'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage presents a series of severe condemnations of kalam (dialectical theology) by early authorities. It begins by stating that most Salaf and some Khalaf disliked and prohibited kalam, logic, and related sciences. The first quote is from Abu Yusuf to Bishr al-Marisi: 'Knowledge of kalam is ignorance, and ignorance of kalam is knowledge.' The author explains that this means either believing kalam to be false is beneficial, or ignoring it preserves one's intellect. Abu Yusuf also says that seeking kalam leads to heresy (tazannuq). Next, al-Shafi'i's harsh ruling is cited: people of kalam should be beaten and paraded as a punishment for abandoning the Quran and Sunnah. Al-Shafi'i also says that only hadith and fiqh are true knowledge, and that meeting Allah with any sin except shirk is better than meeting Him with any kalam. He adds that he witnessed heretical statements from people of kalam. Then a fatwa from the author's school is mentioned: bequests for scholars exclude mutakallimun, and books of kalam should be sold. The author endorses this fatwa, arguing that one cannot reach the science of usul (principles) without following the Prophet. The passage concludes with a poem stating that all knowledge is subordinate to the knowledge of the Prophet.

Key Terms
أهل الكلام
الكتاب والسنة
أهل البدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That al-Shafi'i forbade all intellectual discussion about religion.
Correction: Al-Shafi'i condemned the kalam of innovators that contradicted the Quran and Sunnah, not all theological reflection. He himself engaged in legal reasoning and debated.

Checkpoint
According to al-Shafi'i, which of the following is better than meeting Allah with any part of kalam?
A) Meeting Allah with shirk
B) Meeting Allah with every sin except shirk
C) Meeting Allah with only good deeds
D) Meeting Allah without any belief

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i's harsh condemnation reflects the view that kalam leads to abandoning the Quran and Sunnah and is more dangerous than major sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading al-Shafi'i's statement that meeting Allah with any sin except shirk is better than engaging in kalam, what is one area of your religious learning that you prioritize more than direct engagement with the Quran and Sunnah? What step will you take this week to shift your focus back to the primary sources?
?
Al-Shafi'i said that abandoning the Book and Sunnah leads to kalam. Is there any aspect of your deen where you rely more on human reasoning or secondary sources than on the revealed texts? How will you correct this?
?
The punishment described for people of kalam is public humiliation. Reflect on your own attitude: when you hear views that differ from the Salaf, do you feel urged to debate them using rational arguments, or do you turn back to the Quran and Sunnah? What does your reaction reveal about your heart?

The Fatwa Against Kalam Books and the Poem
Fatwa against kalam books and concluding poem

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the practical implications of the early condemnation: the fatwa to exclude mutakallimun from bequests and to sell books of kalam, and the poetic conclusion.

Core Idea
Kalam books should be sold; all knowledge serves the Prophet's knowledge.

The passage concludes with a fatwa from the Hanafi school: bequests for scholars do not include mutakallimun, and books of kalam should be sold. The author endorses this and adds a poem stating that all knowledge is subordinate to the knowledge of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the fatwa and its reasoning
Read the Arabic and translation. The fatwa is about bequests and selling books of kalam.
This fatwa shows the practical effect of the condemnation.
2
Understand the author's support
The author calls this 'commendable speech' and argues that one cannot reach usul without following the Prophet.
3
Examine the poem
Read the poem: 'O you who go out seeking knowledge, every knowledge is a servant to the knowledge of the Messenger...'
This reinforces the primacy of prophetic knowledge.
4
Connect to the broader lesson
Consider how this passage concludes the argument against kalam: even the study of usul (principles) must be based on following the Prophet, not independent reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the fatwa means all books of kalam are to be destroyed.
Correction: The fatwa says to sell them, not destroy. The point is to prevent their study and use, but they can be sold.

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa cited by the author, what should be done with kalam books that are part of a bequest?
A) They should be kept and studied
B) They should be burned
C) They should be sold
D) They should be given to the mutakallimun

Key Takeaway
The practical consequence of condemning kalam was to exclude its practitioners from bequests and to remove their books from circulation, emphasizing the primacy of following the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a theological issue, do you instinctively turn to rational proofs or the Qur'an and Sunnah? The poem declares that every knowledge is a servant to the knowledge of the Messenger. Is your study of usul al-din truly subservient to revelation, or have you made your intellect the judge? Repent and realign your priorities.
?
The fatwa excludes mutakallimun from bequests. While that is a legal ruling, it reveals the gravity of prioritizing kalam. Have you ever considered that your own approach to theology might be more influenced by human reasoning than by prophetic guidance? Take a moment to examine your bookshelf—what percentage are commentaries on the Qur'an and hadith versus works of kalam? Commit to a change.
?
The line 'how have you neglected the knowledge of the principle of principles?' is directed at you. Are you neglecting the Prophet's knowledge? In your daily life, when you seek to understand your faith, do you go straight to the sources or to the speculations of theologians? Decide today to make the Sunnah your first reference for every belief.

Al-Suyuti's Prohibition of Philosophy and Logic
Al-Suyuti quotes a ruling prohibiting philosophy and logic based on consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the basis and scope of al-Suyuti's ruling that philosophy and logic are forbidden.

Core Idea
Al-Suyuti declared logic and philosophy forbidden based on a claimed consensus of early and later scholars.

This lesson presents a direct quotation from the great scholar Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti, who issues a firm ruling on the study of philosophy and logic. He grounds his opinion on the consensus of the Salaf and most exegetes, and names prominent scholars who supported this view. The passage also highlights an important shift in al-Ghazali's position. Read on to see the evidence and the names behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without interpreting. Then read the translation to grasp the literal meaning before analysis.
Notice the dense list of names and the reporting structure.
2
Identify the key claim and evidence
Al-Suyuti states his ruling is based on consensus of the Salaf and most later exegetes. He then lists scholars who explicitly supported this.
Note the named scholars: Ibn al-Salah, al-Nawawi, al-Qazwini, al-Silafi, Ibn Rushd.
3
Consider the significance of al-Ghazali's retraction
Al-Suyuti reports that al-Ghazali initially praised logic but later returned to prohibiting it. Reflect on why this might strengthen the argument.
Al-Ghazali is a major authority; his change of view is noteworthy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال شيخ مشايخنا الجلال السيوطي: «إنه يحرم علوم الفلسفة كالمنطق لإجماع السلف وأكثر المفسرين المعتبرين من الخلف، وممن صرح بذلك ابن الصلاح والنووي وخلق لا يحصون، وقد جمعت في تحريمه كتابا نقلت فيه نصوص الأئمة في الحط عليه وذكر الحافظ سراج الدين القزويني من الحنفية في كتاب ألفه في تحريمه أن الغزالي رجع إلى تحريمه بعد ثنائه عليه في أول "المنتقى"، وجزم السلفي من أصحابنا وابن رشد من المالكية، بأن المشتغل به لا تقبل روايته انتهى.
And the Shaykh of our shaykhs, al-Jalal al-Suyuti, said: 'It is forbidden to study the sciences of philosophy such as logic, due to the consensus of the Salaf and most of the respected exegetes among the Khalaf. Among those who explicitly stated this are Ibn al-Salah, al-Nawawi, and countless others. I have compiled a book on its prohibition, transmitting the texts of the imams in denouncing it. And al-Hafiz Siraj al-Din al-Qazwini from the Hanafis mentioned in a book he wrote on its prohibition that al-Ghazali returned to the view of its prohibition after having praised it in the beginning of "al-Muntaqa". And al-Silafi from our companions and Ibn Rushd from the Malikis asserted that the practitioner of it does not have his narration accepted. End.'
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage records a fatwa from Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti declaring the study of philosophy and logic to be haram (forbidden). He bases this on the consensus (ijma') of the Salaf and most respected later exegetes (mufassirin). He names individual scholars who explicitly stated this, including Ibn al-Salah, al-Nawawi, and many others. Al-Suyuti also composed a book gathering the texts of the imams on this matter. He mentions that al-Ghazali initially praised logic but later retracted and declared it forbidden. Additionally, two scholars—al-Silafi (from the Shafi'is?) and Ibn Rushd (the Maliki judge, not the philosopher)—assert that a person who engages in logic and philosophy cannot have his hadith narrations accepted.

Key Terms
فلسفة
منطق
تحريم
إجماع السلف
السيوطي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Suyuti only prohibits philosophy, not logic, because logic is a tool for kalam.
Correction: The passage explicitly includes logic: 'It is forbidden to study the sciences of philosophy such as logic.'

Checkpoint
According to al-Suyuti, who among the following returned to the prohibition of logic after initially praising it?
A) Ibn al-Salah
B) Al-Nawawi
C) Al-Ghazali
D) Ibn Rushd

Key Takeaway
Al-Suyuti's prohibition of logic and philosophy is grounded in a claimed consensus and supported by many scholars, including al-Ghazali's retraction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Suyuti claims a consensus against logic and philosophy. Have you ever unquestioningly accepted a religious ruling without verifying its evidence? How does this challenge your dependence on scholars versus personal investigation?
?
The passage mentions that even al-Ghazali retracted his support for logic after initially praising it. Is there an area of knowledge you have changed your mind about? What would it take for you to admit you were wrong on a deeply held belief?
?
These scholars said that one who practices ‘philosophy and logic’ cannot have his narrations accepted. Does this making you reconsider the tools and methodologies you use to learn about your faith? How can you ensure your pursuit of knowledge is aligned with divine guidance?

Prohibition of Kalam and Philosophy by Al-Suyuti and Others
Al-Suyuti states the prohibition of philosophy and kalam with supporting citations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classical Sunni position that philosophy and logic are forbidden based on scholarly consensus, as argued by Al-Suyuti and others.

Core Idea
All knowledge is servant to prophetic knowledge; philosophy and logic are forbidden by consensus.

This lesson presents a classical Sunni position that studying philosophy and logic is prohibited. Al-Suyuti, citing a wide range of scholars, argues that these disciplines lead away from the prophetic path. The passage includes a powerful poetic reminder of the primacy of prophetic knowledge and reports that even al-Ghazali eventually recanted his earlier endorsement of logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and poem
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the poetic emphasis that all knowledge serves prophetic knowledge.
The poem sets the tone for the entire argument.
2
Identify the authorities cited
Notice which scholars are mentioned: Ibn al-Salah, al-Nawawi, al-Qazwini, al-Silafi, Ibn Rushd. Note their specific contributions.
These names anchor the consensus claim.
3
Trace the argument's progression
The passage moves from a general principle (following the Messenger) to a specific prohibition (philosophy/logic), supported by consensus and individual scholars, ending with a ruling on acceptance of narrations.
Understanding this flow helps grasp the rhetorical structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر ذلك بمعناه في الفتاوى" "الظهيرية وهو كلام مستحسن عند أرباب العقول إذ كيف يرام الوصول إلى علم الأصول بغير اتباع ما جاء به الرسول. والله در القائل في هذا المقول: أيها المغتدي لتطلب علما كل علم عبد لعلم الرسول تطلب العلم كي تصحح أصلا كيف أغفلت علم أصل الأصول وقد قال شيخ مشايخنا الجلال السيوطي: «إنه يحرم علوم الفلسفة كالمنطق لإجماع السلف وأكثر المفسرين المعتبرين من الخلف، وممن صرح بذلك ابن الصلاح والنووي وخلق لا يحصون، وقد جمعت في تحريمه كتابا نقلت فيه نصوص الأئمة في الحط عليه وذكر الحافظ سراج الدين القزويني من الحنفية في كتاب ألفه في تحريمه أن الغزالي رجع إلى تحريمه بعد ثنائه عليه في أول "المنتقى"، وجزم السلفي من أصحابنا وابن رشد من المالكية، بأن المشتغل به لا تقبل روايته انتهى.
He mentioned that in meaning in the fatwas "al-Zahiriyyah", and it is commendable speech in the view of people of intellect, for how can reaching the science of usul be desired without following what the Messenger brought? By Allah, how excellent is the poet in this saying: 'O you who strive to seek knowledge, every knowledge is a servant to the knowledge of the Messenger. You seek knowledge to correct a foundation, how have you neglected the foundation of foundations?' And the shaykh of our shaykhs, al-Jalal al-Suyuti, said: 'Indeed, the sciences of philosophy, such as logic, are forbidden due to the consensus of the Salaf and most of the respected exegetes among the Khalaf. Among those who explicitly stated that are Ibn al-Salah, al-Nawawi, and countless others. I have compiled a book on its prohibition in which I transmitted the texts of the imams regarding disparaging it. Al-Hafiz Siraj al-Din al-Qazwini of the Hanafis mentioned in a book he authored on its prohibition that al-Ghazali recanted to its prohibition after praising it earlier in "al-Muntaqa". Al-Silafi of our companions and Ibn Rushd of the Malikis affirmed that the one who occupies himself with it, his narration is not accepted.' End.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is an argument supporting the prohibition of kalam and philosophy. It begins with a general commendation of following the Messenger, then quotes a poem emphasizing that all knowledge is subservient to prophetic knowledge. It then cites al-Suyuti's explicit fatwa declaring philosophy and logic forbidden, supported by consensus of the Salaf and many later exegetes. The passage lists prominent scholars who affirmed this, including Ibn al-Salah, al-Nawawi, and others. It mentions a book written on its prohibition and notes that al-Ghazali is reported to have recanted his earlier praise of logic. Finally, it states that according to al-Silafi and Ibn Rushd, the one who engages in such sciences is not accepted as a reliable narrator. The passage presents this as a complete position without yet addressing counterarguments.

Key Terms
علوم الفلسفة
المنطق
الكلام
السلف
الغزالي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Philosophy and logic are universally permissible in Islam and al-Ghazali consistently approved of them.
Correction: Al-Suyuti shows a consensus of Salaf and later scholars that they are forbidden, and al-Ghazali recanted his earlier praise.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Ghazali do regarding the prohibition of logic?
A) He consistently affirmed its permissibility.
B) He recanted to its prohibition after initially praising it.
C) He never mentioned logic in his works.
D) He only prohibited it for commoners.

Key Takeaway
The study of philosophy and logic is forbidden by consensus of the early Muslims and many later scholars, and even al-Ghazali eventually retracted his endorsement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that al-Ghazali himself recanted his earlier endorsement of logic after realizing its harm. Is there any intellectual habit, course of study, or teacher you follow that you have not critically examined in light of the Quran and Sunnah? Will you honestly re-evaluate it this week, even if it means changing direction?
?
The scholars declared that engagement in philosophy and logic makes one's narration unreliable. Does your heart tremble at the thought of standing before Allah with knowledge acquired from sources He has prohibited? If you have studied philosophy or logic without knowing its ruling, will you repent and abandon it now, seeking only the knowledge that serves the Prophet's message?
?
You claim to seek knowledge, but do you prioritize the 'foundation of foundations'—the prophetic revelation—over your own intellectual curiosity? What is one specific step you will take tomorrow to align your pursuit of knowledge with the hierarchy taught in this passage: all knowledge as servant to the knowledge of the Messenger?

Extreme Views on Kalam: Prohibition vs Obligation
Al-Ghazali presents the extreme views on kalam and the arguments for prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two extreme positions on ilm al-kalam and the arguments of the early imams for prohibiting it.

Core Idea
Rulings on kalam are debated; early Imams saw it as dangerous innovation.

Al-Ghazali begins his nuanced treatment by presenting the question of kalam's ruling and the extremes people have adopted. He outlines both the view that it is a forbidden innovation and the view that it is an obligation and the best worship. He also relays the arguments of the hadith scholars and early imams who prohibited it, including the prophetic condemnation of excessive argumentation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how al-Ghazali frames the debate between two extremes.
Pay attention to the question that sets up the discussion.
2
Identify the two extreme views
Look for the two opposing positions: one declaring kalam a forbidden innovation, the other an obligation and best worship. Note the imams associated with the prohibition view.
Imams listed: al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad, Sufyan, etc.
3
Analyze the prohibitionist arguments
Find the two main arguments: the Companions' silence about kalam and the Prophet's hadith against 'mutanaṭṭiʿūn' (those who go to extremes). Ask yourself why these arguments were convincing.
The hadith is: 'Hajja al-mutanaṭṭiʿūn' – the extremists are destroyed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد فصل الإمام حجة الإسلام" في "إحياء العلوم" هذا المرام حيث قال: «فإن قلت: فعلم الجدل والكلام مذموم كعلم النجوم أو هو مباح أو مندوب ؟ فاعلم أن للناس في هذا غلوّا وإسرافاً في أطراف فمن قائل: إنه بدعة وحرام وإن العبد أن يلقى الله بكل ذنب سوى الشرك له من أن يلقاه بالكلام ومن قائل: إنه ،فرض إما على الكفاية وإما على الأعيان، وإنه أفضل العبادات وأكمل القربات، فإنه تحقيق لعلم التوحيد ونضال عن دين الله المجيد». قال: «وإلى التحريم ذهب الشافعي ومحمد ومالك وأحمد بن حنبل وسفيان وجميع أئمة الحديث من السلف رضي الله عنهم». وساق عنهم ألفاظاً عن هؤلاء، وأنهم قالوا: «ما سكت عنه عن الصحابة مع أنهم أعرف بالحقائق وأفصح في ترتيب الألفاظ من سائر الخلائق إلا لما يتولد منه الشر»، ولذا قال عليه الصلوة والسلام: (هلك المتنطعون) (1) أي المتعمقون في البحث واحتجوا أيضاً بأن ذلك لو كان من الدين لكان أهم ما يأمر به رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، ويعلم طريقه ويثني على أربابه ، ثم ذكر بقية استدلالهم. ثم ذكر استدلال الفريق الآخر إلى أن قال: فإن قلت : فما المختار عندك؟ فأجاب بالتفصيل فقال: «فيه منفعة وفيه مضرة، فهو باعتبار منفعته في وقت الانتفاع حلال أو مندوب أو واجب كما يقتضيه الحال، وهو باعتبار مضرته في وقت الاستضرار ومحله حرام». قال: «فأما مضرته فإثارة الشبهات وتحريك العقائد وإزلتها عن الجزم والتصميم وذلك مما يحصل بالابتداء، ورجوعه بالدليل المشكوك فيه وتختلف فيه الأشخاص، فهذا ضرره في اعتقاد المحق. وله ضرر في تأكيد اعتقاد المبتدعة وتثبيتها في صدورهم بحيث تنبعث دواعيهم ويشتد حرصهم على الإصرار عليه ولكن هذا الضرر بواسطة التعصب الذي يثور عن وأما منفعته فقد يظن أن فائدته كشف الحقائق لديه ومعرفتها على ما هي عليه وهيهات فليس في الكلام وفاء بهذا المطلب الشريف، ولعل التخبيط والتضليل أكثر من الكشف والتعريف». قال: «وهذا إذا سمعته من محدث أو حشوي ربما خطر ببالك أن الناس أعداء ما جهلوا، ممن خبر الكلام ثم قلاه بعد حقيقة الخبرة وبعد التغلغل فيه إلى منتهى درجة المتكلمين، وجاوز ذلك إلى التعمق في علوم أخرى سوى نوع الكلام، وتحقق أن الطريق إلى حقائق المعرفة من هذا الوجه مسدود. ولعمري لا ينفك الكلام عن کشف وتعريف وإيضاح لبعض الأمور ولكن على الندور، انتهى.
And the Imam Hujjat al-Islam detailed this matter in "Ihya' 'Ulum al-Din" where he said: 'If you say: Is the science of debate (jadal) and kalam blameworthy like astrology, or is it permissible or recommended? Know that people have gone to extremes and excess in this matter. Some say: It is an innovation and forbidden, and that a servant meeting Allah with every sin except shirk is better for him than meeting Him with kalam. Others say: It is an obligation, either collective or individual, and it is the best of acts of worship and the most complete of acts of drawing near to Allah, because it is the realization of the science of tawhid and striving for the religion of Allah, the Glorious.' He said: 'And the view of prohibition was held by al-Shafi'i, Muhammad [al-Shaybani], Malik, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, Sufyan, and all the hadith scholars among the Salaf, may Allah be pleased with them.' And he narrated from them statements about these, that they said: 'The Companions remained silent about it even though they were most knowledgeable of realities and most eloquent in arranging words of all creation, only because of the evil that arises from it.' Hence the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'The mutanaṭṭi‘ūn (those who go to extremes) are destroyed'— meaning those who delve deeply into research. And they also argued that if this were part of the religion, it would be the most important thing the Messenger of Allah commanded, taught its way, and praised its people.' Then he mentioned the rest of their arguments. Then he mentioned the arguments of the other group until he said: 'If you say: What is your chosen opinion? He answered in detail saying: 'It has benefit and it has harm. In terms of its benefit at a time of benefiting, it is lawful, recommended, or obligatory as the situation requires. And in terms of its harm at a time of harm and in a place of harm, it is forbidden.' He said: 'As for its harm: stirring up doubts, shaking beliefs, and removing them from certainty and firmness—this happens at the beginning, and [the ability to] return to [certainty] via questionable evidence varies among individuals. This is its harm in the belief of the one who is correct. It also has a harm in strengthening the belief of the innovators and fixing it in their hearts such that their motivations arise and their eagerness to persist in it intensifies. But this harm is due to the fanaticism that arises from... As for its benefit: one might think that its benefit is the uncovering of realities and knowing them as they truly are—far from it! For kalam does not fulfill this noble aim; rather, confusion and misguidance are more frequent than uncovering and clarification.' He said: 'If you hear this from a hadith scholar or a Hashawi, it might cross your mind that people are enemies of what they do not know—but [this comes] from one who has experienced kalam, then despised it after true experience and after delving deeply into it to the furthest degree of the mutakallimun, and surpassed that to delving into other sciences besides kalam, and realized that the path to the realities of knowledge through this avenue is blocked. By my life, kalam is not free from uncovering, defining, and clarifying some matters, but only rarely.' End.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is al-Ghazali's detailed treatment of the ruling of kalam. It begins with a question (objection): is kalam blameworthy, permissible, or recommended? He then describes the extreme views: some say it is a forbidden innovation, others say it is an obligation and the best worship. He notes that the prohibition view was held by major early imams, citing their argument that the Companions avoided it due to its potential for evil, and that the Prophet condemned excessive argumentation. After presenting both sides, al-Ghazali gives his own detailed answer (the 'chosen opinion'): kalam has both benefit and harm, so its ruling depends on context—it can be lawful, recommended, or even obligatory when beneficial, but forbidden when harmful. He then elaborates on the harms: stirring doubts, weakening certainty (especially for the truth-holder), and strengthening the conviction of innovators through fanaticism. The benefit is supposedly uncovering truths, but al-Ghazali is skeptical, saying confusion is more common. He concludes by quoting someone who, after deep expertise in kalam and other sciences, concluded that the path to knowledge through kalam is blocked, and that any benefit is rare. Thus, al-Ghazali offers a nuanced position that avoids blanket permission or prohibition.

Key Terms
الكلام
الجدل
المتنطعون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ghazali believed kalam is absolutely forbidden.
Correction: Al-Ghazali is here reporting the views of others; his own detailed answer follows and is context-dependent.

Checkpoint
According to the early imams, why did the Companions remain silent about kalam?
A) Because they were not eloquent enough.
B) Because it was a secret science.
C) Because of the evil that arises from it.
D) Because they did not know about it.

Key Takeaway
Early Islamic scholars held that ilm al-kalam was a dangerous innovation, despite some considering it an obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a religious practice that is debated among scholars, do you tend to immediately side with the stricter view or the more lenient one? What in this lesson challenges that tendency?
?
The Prophet ﷺ warned against 'going to extremes' (المتنطعون). Where in your own life—whether in worship, study, or interactions—do you see yourself crossing into excessive depth or zeal at the cost of balance?
?
If you were to defend your faith (as the second group says about kalam), would your defense be more rooted in heartfelt certainty or in argumentative skill based on this lesson's warning?

Al-Ghazali's Nuanced Ruling: Kalam's Benefit and Harm
Al-Ghazali gives a nuanced ruling on kalam based on context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ghazali's context-dependent ruling on ilm al-kalam based on its benefits and harms.

Core Idea
Kalam is neither always allowed nor always forbidden; its ruling depends on time, place, and consequences.

After presenting the extreme views, al-Ghazali gives his own detailed answer. He argues that kalam has both benefit and harm, so its ruling varies: it can be lawful, recommended, or even obligatory when beneficial, but forbidden when harmful. He elaborates on the harms of stirring doubts and the limited benefit of uncovering truths.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ghazali's answer
Read the Arabic text of his answer, then the translation. Note that he begins with a clear principle: kalam has benefit and harm.
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on the situation.
2
Identify the two aspects: benefit and harm
Find where al-Ghazali lists the harms (stirring doubts, shaking beliefs, strengthening innovators) and the benefit (possible clarification, though rarely).
Pay attention to his skeptical tone regarding the benefit.
3
Understand the context-dependence
Al-Ghazali says the ruling changes based on time and place of benefit vs harm. Consider how this avoids both extremes.
This shows his balanced approach.

Source Text

Commentary

The benefit is supposedly uncovering truths, but al-Ghazali is skeptical, saying confusion is more common. He concludes by quoting someone who, after deep expertise in kalam and other sciences, concluded that the path to knowledge through kalam is blocked, and that any benefit is rare. Thus, al-Ghazali offers a nuanced position that avoids blanket permission or prohibition.

?

?
Al-Ghazali says that kalam can strengthen the beliefs of innovators by increasing their fanaticism. Is there a belief you hold so defensively that you refuse to examine it critically, fearing it might weaken? Would you be willing to test it for the sake of sincerity, even at the risk of doubt?
?
The path to knowledge through kalam is described as 'blocked' by al-Ghazali. Where do you truly seek certainty—in intellectual debate or in something else? If kalam only rarely clarifies, where will you invest your limited time to deepen your understanding of God?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
4 min
Imams Shafi'i and Malik Condemn Kalam
The author transmits condemnatory statements from Shafi'i and Malik regarding those engaged in kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two major Sunni imams explicitly condemned engagement in kalam, equating it with loss of religion and following desires.

Core Idea
Kalam is condemned by early authorities as a path of desires, not faith.

Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik, two towering figures of early Sunni Islam, are often quoted by opponents of kalam to show that theological speculation is a dangerous innovation. In this passage, their harsh statements are transmitted and interpreted. We will examine what they said and why it matters for the debate over kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the statements of al-Shafi'i
Read the first two statements attributed to al-Shafi'i. Notice the strong language: 'has no religion' and 'flee from it as from a lion.'
These are from known works of al-Shafi'i, though their authenticity is debated.
2
Read Malik's statement and its interpretation
Read Malik's ruling on the testimony of 'people of desires' and the interpretation that this refers to kalam practitioners.
The interpretation by some of Malik's companions is key to understanding the intended target.
3
Reflect on the overall stance
Consider why these imams condemned kalam so severely. What does this tell us about the early Sunni perspective on theological speculation?
This helps connect the passage to broader methodological debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الشافعي رحمه الله: إذا سمعت الرجل يقول: الاسم هو المسمى أو غير المسمى، فاشهد بأنه من أهل الكلام ولا دين له. وقال أيضاً: «لو علم الناس ما في هذا الكلام من الأهواء لفروا منه فرارهم من الأسد». وقال مالك رحمه الله: «لا تجوز شهادة أهل البدع والأهواء». فقال بعض أصحابه تأويل ذلك: «إنه أراد بأهل الأهواء أهل الكلام على أي مذهب كانوا».
And al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'When you hear a man saying: the name is the named or other than the named, then bear witness that he is from the people of kalam and has no religion.' And he also said: 'If people knew what is in this kalam of desires, they would flee from it as they flee from a lion.' And Malik, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'The testimony of the people of innovations and desires is not permissible.' Some of his companions said as an interpretation of that: 'He meant by 'people of desires' the people of kalam, on whatever school they were.'
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage reports two authoritative statements condemning kalam. First, al-Shafi'i says that if you hear someone debating whether the name (ism) is identical to the named (musamma) or distinct—a classic kalam issue—then testify that he is from the people of kalam and has no religion. This is a very strong condemnation, equating involvement in such theological subtleties with loss of religion. Second, al-Shafi'i adds that if people realized how much personal desire (ahwa) is involved in kalam, they would flee from it like from a lion. Then Malik is quoted as saying that the testimony (shahada) of people of innovations and desires is not acceptable. Some of Malik's own followers interpret 'people of desires' as referring to the people of kalam, regardless of which specific school (madhhab) of kalam they follow. This shows that the condemnation is general: the very engagement in kalam is seen as a form of following desires, invalidating one's religious testimony.

Key Terms
الاسم
المسمى
أهل الكلام
الأهواء
أهل البدع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only specific positions in kalam are condemned, like the name/named debate.
Correction: Al-Shafi'i's statement targets the entire field: if someone engages in such debates, they are labeled as 'people of kalam' with no religion. The condemnation is general.

Checkpoint
According to al-Shafi'i, what should be one's conclusion upon hearing someone debate whether the name is the same as the named?
A) That the person is a knowledgeable scholar.
B) That the person is from the people of kalam and has no religion.
C) That the person is a follower of his own school.
D) That the person is a liar.

Key Takeaway
Early Sunni imams like al-Shafi'i and Malik condemned kalam in the strongest terms, viewing it as a dangerous path of personal desire that invalidates one's religious standing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear debates about theological details—like the difference between a name and a named—does your heart feel drawn to join in or afraid? Al-Shafi'i says that if you knew what was in it, you would flee from it like from a lion. What does your reaction reveal about your attachment to such discussions? Will you walk away the next time your mind is tempted to enter a theological argument?
?
Malik considered engagement in kalam sufficient to invalidate one's testimony. Your testimony on the Day of Judgment is at stake. Are there conversations or intellectual pursuits in your life that you have justified as 'harmless' or 'defending the faith,' which in reality might be feeding your own desires? Are you willing to abandon any discussion that the early imams would have condemned, no matter how reasonable it seems?
?
The imams' strongest warnings are against the hidden desires that kalam stirs up. Think of a recent discussion or argument you had about religion that became heated or prideful. Can you honestly say that desire for victory or intellectual superiority was not present? What would it look like for you to flee from that desire today, not just externally but in your heart?

Ahmad ibn Hanbal's Condemnation of Kalam
The author reports Ahmad ibn Hanbal's harsh condemnation and his treatment of al-Muhasibi over kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ahmad ibn Hanbal's harsh condemnation of kalam and his rationale for avoiding even refutations of innovation.

Core Idea
For Imam Ahmad, even refuting innovation can spread the disease.

This lesson presents a striking report from Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal, one of the greatest Salaf Imams. He did not merely condemn kalam but took extreme measures, even shunning a pious scholar for writing a refutation. His reasoning reveals a deep concern about the subtle harms of engaging with falsehood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation slowly. Notice the strong language Ahmad uses: 'zanadiqa' (heretics) and 'daghil' (disease).
These are very strong terms in Islamic discourse.
2
Understand the general condemnation
Ahmad makes two general statements about kalam. Identify them and reflect on their severity.
He says kalam scholars are heretics and that anyone who looks into kalam develops a spiritual disease.
3
Analyze the al-Muhasibi incident
Read why Ahmad abandoned al-Muhasibi. What was his objection to writing a refutation?
Ahmad feared that even refuting innovation exposes people to doubts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروي عن أحمد بن حنبل رحمه الله أنه قال: «علماء الكلام زنادقة». وقال أيضاً: «لا يصلح صاحب الكلام أبداً ولا تكاد ترى أحداً نظر في الكلام إلا وفي قلبه دغل». ولقد بالغ فيه حتى هجر الحارث بن أسد المحاسبي مع زهده وورعه بسبب تصنيفه كتابا في الرد على المبتدعة وقال: «ويحك ألست تحكي بدعتهم أولاً ثم تردّ عليهم؟ ألست تحمل الناس بتصنيفك على مطالعة البدعة والتفكر في الشبهة فيدعوهم ذلك إلى الرأي والبحث والفتنة؟».
And it is narrated from Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may Allah have mercy on him, that he said: 'The scholars of kalam are heretics (zanadiqa).' And he also said: 'The person of kalam never becomes upright, and you hardly ever see anyone who looked into kalam but that there is a disease (daghil) in his heart.' And he went to extremes in it such that he abandoned al-Harith ibn Asad al-Muhasibi, despite his asceticism and piety, because of his authorship of a book refuting the innovators (al-mubtadi'a), saying: 'Woe to you! Do you not first narrate their innovation and then refute them? Do you not, by your writing, lead people to study innovation and reflect upon the doubt, which calls them to opinion, research, and tribulation?'
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage presents the view of Ahmad ibn Hanbal, one of the most prominent Imams of the Salaf and founder of the Hanbali school. He is reported to have said that 'the scholars of kalam are zanadiqa'—a very strong term meaning heretics or hypocrites. He also said that a person who engages in kalam never becomes righteous (la yasluh) and that anyone who looks into kalam has a disease (daghil) in his heart, meaning spiritual sickness or hypocrisy. The author then mentions that Ahmad went so far as to abandon al-Harith al-Muhasibi, despite the latter's extreme asceticism and piety, because al-Muhasibi wrote a book refuting the innovators. Ahmad's objection was that by writing such a refutation, al-Muhasibi first quotes and spreads the innovation, then refutes it, thereby exposing people to doubts and leading them into opinion (ra'y), research (bahth), and fitna (tribulation). This reflects a methodology of complete avoidance of even refutations, lest the exposure cause harm.

Key Terms
زنادقة
دغل
المحاسبي
الرد على المبتدعة
الشبهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Writing refutations of heresy is always praiseworthy and without risk.
Correction: Ahmad ibn Hanbal shows that even refutations can be harmful if they propagate the falsehood by quoting it first, leading people to study it and fall into doubt.

Checkpoint
Why did Ahmad ibn Hanbal abandon al-Muhasibi despite his piety?
A) Because al-Muhasibi was a heretic.
B) Because al-Muhasibi wrote a book refuting innovators, and Ahmad believed that spreading even the refutation leads to harm.
C) Because al-Muhasibi used kalam in his refutation.
D) Because al-Muhasibi did not follow Ahmad's school.

Key Takeaway
Ahmad ibn Hanbal believed that even refutations of innovation could lead people into doubt and fitna, so he avoided them entirely.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever engaged with a doubtful belief, even to refute it, and felt a lingering trace in your heart? After this lesson, what will you do to protect your heart from the disease of kalam, as Ahmad taught?
?
Imam Ahmad avoided even quoting falsehood for refutation. When you speak about false beliefs, do you guard your tongue and heart from their influence? How will you change your approach starting today?
?
The scholars of kalam are called heretics by Ahmad. Are there any 'kalam-like' activities in your own life that you justify as 'just refuting'? Will you abandon them for the sake of your heart's purity, even if it means staying silent?

Objections Against Kalam: Testimonies of Regret
The author presents testimonies from scholars who warned against kalam and regretted it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why many prominent Islamic scholars warned against speculative theology (kalam) and advocated a return to the Quran and simple faith.

Core Idea
Kalam leads to confusion; the Quran is sufficient.

This lesson presents a series of testimonies from renowned scholars who engaged deeply with kalam and later expressed regret, confusion, or a turn to the Quran and hadith. The author uses their words as evidence that speculative theology ultimately leads to doubt and misguidance, while the Quran provides clear guidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic sufficiency argument
Begin with the passage stating that all established beliefs are in the Quran and Sunnah, with Quranic verses supporting sufficiency. This sets the foundation for the critique of kalam.
Verses from Surah Ibrahim and Al-Ankabut are cited.
2
Examine the testimonies of al-Ghazali and al-Razi
Study the quotes from al-Ghazali (who turned to hadith) and al-Razi (who wrote poetry lamenting the futility of theological research). They are key examples of scholars who abandoned kalam.
Al-Razi's poem is particularly powerful.
3
Review warnings by al-Juwayni and others
Note al-Juwayni's advice against kalam and his death on a simple creed. Also consider the later figures like al-Khusraw Shahi and al-Khunji who expressed uncertainty.
Al-Juwayni said he died on the creed of old women.
4
Understand the remedy offered
The passage ends with a supplication for steadfastness, indicating that the cure for the confusion of kalam is turning to Allah with humble prayer.
The supplication is from the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Source Text

والصلاة والصوم كان جاهلاً عنها وساكتاً فيها مع أن جميع العقائد الثابتة موجودة في الكتاب قطعيا وفي السنة ظنيا، ولذا قال الله تعالى: ﴿هدَابَكُمْ لِلنَّاسِ [إبراهيم:٥٢] أي القرآن كفاية لهم في الموعظة في أمر معاشهم ومعادهم. وقال الله تعالى: ﴿اَوَلَمْ يَكْفِهِمْ أَنَا أَنْزَلْنَا عَلَيْكَ الْكِتَبَ يُتْلَى عَلَيْهِمْ [العنكبوت: ٥١] أي القرآن تدوم تلاوته عليهم في كل مكان وزمان مع علمهم بأنك أمي لا تكتب ولا تقرأ.
ومنها: أن مآل علم الكلام والجدل إلى الحيرة في الحال والضلال والشك في المآل كما قال ابن رشد الحفيد وهو من أعلم الناس بمذهب الفلاسفة ومقالاتهم في كتابه "تهافت التهافت" ومن الذي قال في الإلهيات شيئا يُعتد به وكذلك الآمدي أفضل أهل زمانه واقف في المسائل الكبار حائر. وكذلك الغزالي انتهى آخر أمره إلى التوقف والحيرة في المسائل الكلامية، ثم أعرض عن تلك الطرق وأقبل على أحاديث رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فمات والبخاري على صدره. وكذا الرازي قال في كتابه الذي صنفه في أقسام الذات:

عقال وغاية سعي
العالمين ضلال وأرواحنا في وحشة من جسومنا و حاصل دنيانا أذى ووبال
ولم نستفد بحثنا طول عمرنا من
سوى أن جمعنا فيه قيل وقالوا
ولقد تأملت الطرق الكلامية والمناهج الفلسفية فما رأيتها تشفي عليلا ولا تروي غليلا، ورأيت أقرب الطرق طريق القرآن اقرأ في الإثبات الرَّحْمنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ﴾ [طه: ٥] و إِلَيْهِ يَصْعَدُ الْكَلِمُ الطَّيِّبُ ﴾ [فاطر: ١٠] واقرأ في النفي: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْ [الشورى: ۱۱] و وَلَا يُحِيطُونَ بِهِ عِلْمًا ﴾ [طه: ١١٠] ثم قال: ومن جرّب مثل تجربتي عرف مثل معرفتي.
وكذا قال الشهرستاني رحمه الله : إنه لم يجد على الفلاسفة والمتكلمين إلا الحيرة والندم
حيث قال :
لعمري لقد طفت المعاهد كلها وسيرت طرفي بين تلك المعالم
فلم أر إلا واضعاً كف حائر
على ذقن أو قارعاً سن نادم
وكذا قال أبو المعالي الجويني: يا أصحابنا لا تشتغلوا بالكلام فلو عرفت أن الكلام يبلغ بي إلى ما بلغ ما اشتغلت .به». وقال عند موته: «لقد خضت البحر الخضم وخليت أهل الإسلام وعلومهم ودخلت في الذي نهوني عنه والآن فإن لم يتداركني ربي برحمته فالويل لابن الجويني وها أنا ذا أموت على عقيدة أمي أو قال على عقيدة عجائز أهل نيسابور».
وكذا قال الخسرو شاهي وكان من أجل تلامذة فخر الدين الرازي لبعض الفضلاء ودخل عليه يوما ما تعتقده؟ قال : ما يعتقده المسلمون فقال : وأنت منشرح الصدر لذلك مستيقن به؟ أو كما قال، فقال: نعم، فقال: اشكر الله على هذه النعمة، ولكني والله ما أدري ما أعتقد، بكى حتى أخضل لحيته. وقال الخونجي عند موته ما عرفت مما حصلته شيئا سوى أن الممكن مفتقر إلى المرجح ، ثم قال : الافتقار وصف سلبي، أموت وما عرفت شيئاً.
وقال آخر: أضطجع على فراشي وأضع الملحفة على وجهي وأقابل بين حجج هؤلاء وهؤلاء حتى يطلع الفجر ولم يترجح عندي منها شيء، ومن يصل إلى مثل هذا الحال إن لم يتداركه الله بالرحمة والإقبال تزندق وساء له المآل؛ فالدواء النافع لمثل هذا المرض ما كان طبيب القلوب يتضرع به إلى علام الغيوب ويدعو بقوله: (اللهم يا مقلب القلوب ثبت قلبي على دينك)). وبقوله : ((اللهم فاطر السموات والأرض عالم الغيب والشهادة اهدني لما
And prayer and fasting, one is ignorant of them and silent about them, while all the established beliefs exist in the Book definitively and in the Sunnah probabilistically. Therefore Allah Almighty said: 'A reminder to the people' [Ibrahim:52], meaning the Quran is sufficient for them in exhortation concerning their livelihood and their afterlife. And Allah Almighty said: 'Is it not sufficient for them that We have sent down to you the Book to be recited to them' [Al-Ankabut:51], meaning the Quran is continuously recited to them in every place and time, while they know that you are unlettered, you neither write nor read. And among them [the objections] is that the ultimate outcome of the science of kalam and debate is confusion in the present state and misguidance and doubt in the final outcome, as Ibn Rushd the grandson said—and he is the most knowledgeable of people about the doctrine of the philosophers and their statements in his book 'Tahafut al-Tahafut'—and who said something in metaphysics that is taken into account? And likewise al-Amidi, the best of his time, stopped in the great issues, confused. And likewise al-Ghazali ended his last affair in hesitation and confusion in the theological issues, then he turned away from those paths and turned to the hadiths of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, and died with al-Bukhari on his chest. And likewise al-Razi said in his book which he composed on the divisions of the Essence: 'The ultimate of the advance of intellects is a fetter, and the utmost striving of the learned is misguidance, and our souls are in solitude from our bodies, and the outcome of our world is harm and calamity. And we have not benefited from our research our entire life, except that we collected therein 'they said' and 'they said'. And I have pondered the theological paths and the philosophical methods, and I did not see them curing a sick one nor quenching a thirsty one. And I saw the closest path is the path of the Quran: read in affirmation: 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' [Ta-Ha:5] and 'To Him ascends the good word' [Fatir:10]; and read in negation: 'There is nothing like Him' [Ash-Shura:11] and 'They do not encompass Him in knowledge' [Ta-Ha:110]. Then he said: 'Whoever experiences like my experience knows like my knowledge.' And likewise al-Shahrastani, may God have mercy on him, said: he did not find concerning the philosophers and the mutakallimun except confusion and regret, where he said: 'By my life, I have toured all the institutes and moved my eyes among those landmarks, and I saw only one placing a hand on his chin in confusion, or one gnashing his teeth in regret.' And likewise Abu al-Ma'ali al-Juwayni said: 'O our companions, do not occupy yourselves with kalam, for if I had known that kalam would lead me to what it has led, I would not have occupied myself with it.' And he said at his death: 'I have plunged into the deep sea and left behind the people of Islam and their sciences, and entered into that which they forbade me. And now, if my Lord does not take care of me with His mercy, then woe to Ibn al-Juwayni. And here I am dying upon the creed of my mother—or he said: upon the creed of the old women of Nishapur.' And likewise al-Khusraw Shahi, who was among the greatest students of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, said to some virtuous person who entered upon him one day: 'What do you believe?' He said: 'What the Muslims believe.' So he said: 'And are you at ease of heart for that, certain of it?'—or as he said. So he said: 'Yes.' So he said: 'Thank God for this blessing, but by God I do not know what I believe!' He wept until his beard became wet. And al-Khunji said at his death: 'I have not known from what I have acquired anything except that the contingent is in need of the preponderator.' Then he said: 'Need is a negative attribute. I die and I have known nothing.' And another said: 'I lie down on my bed and place the cover over my face and compare the proofs of these and those until dawn breaks, and nothing has become preponderant with me from them. And whoever reaches such a state, if God does not take care of him with mercy and acceptance, he becomes a heretic and evil is his fate. So the beneficial remedy for such an illness is what the physician of hearts supplicates with to the Knower of the Unseen, and he prays with his saying: 'O Allah, O Turner of hearts, make my heart firm upon Your religion.' And with his saying: 'O Allah, Creator of the heavens and the earth, Knower of the unseen and the witnessed, guide me to what...'
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of objections against the science of kalam (speculative theology) and dialectic (jadal), presented by citing the testimonies of renowned scholars who allegedly regretted their engagement with it. The author begins by stating that the Quran is sufficient and that all established beliefs are definitively in the Quran, then introduces a series of quotations. The first argument is that kalam leads to confusion (hayra) in this life and misguidance/doubt in the afterlife, citing Ibn Rushd al-Hafid (Averroes), al-Amidi, al-Ghazali, and al-Razi. Each scholar is shown expressing regret or concluding that the Quranic approach is superior. Al-Ghazali is said to have turned to hadith and died with Sahih al-Bukhari on his chest. Al-Razi's poetic lament describes intellectual endeavor as futile and misleading, and he concludes that the Quranic method is best. Al-Shahristani is quoted in poetry stating he saw only confusion and regret among philosophers and mutakallimun. Al-Juwayni (Imam al-Haramayn) is reported to have advised against kalam and died on the simple creed of his mother or the old women of Nishapur. Then al-Khusraw Shahi and al-Khunji express uncertainty at death. Finally, an anonymous scholar describes being torn between conflicting proofs, and the passage ends with a supplication for steadfastness. The overall message is a strong caution against speculative theology, urging reliance on Quran and simple faith.

Key Terms
علم الكلام
الجدل
الحيرة
الضلال
المتكلمون
الفلاسفة
الكتاب
السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That these scholars rejected all forms of theology and faith.
Correction: They rejected speculative kalam but affirmed Quranic faith and simple belief, as seen in al-Juwayni's death on the creed of his mother.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Ghazali turn to at the end of his life?
A) Philosophy
B) The hadith of the Prophet
C) Fasting and prayer
D) The opinions of al-Amidi

Key Takeaway
Prominent scholars who engaged deeply in kalam often ended in confusion and regret, urging reliance on the Quran and simple faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever pursued intellectual understanding of your faith to the point where it created doubt in your heart rather than certainty? What would it mean for you to trust that the Quran alone is sufficient for guidance, as these scholars eventually did?
?
Al-Juwayni died saying 'I die upon the creed of my mother' – a simple, unwavering faith. Is your own faith more like that of a child trusting in Allah, or is it tangled in complex arguments that leave you uneasy? What step can you take today to simplify your reliance on Allah?
?
If you were to face death tonight, would you claim certainty about Allah and the Unseen, or would you echo al-Khunji's lament – 'I die and I have known nothing'? What does that reveal about the way you are currently seeking knowledge?
