The Obligation to Follow the Prophet Alone
The author establishes the duty to follow the Prophet and cites verse 4:65.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the absolute obligation to follow the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Quranic proof for it, as well as the error of those who seek judgment elsewhere.

Core Idea
True faith demands complete submission to the Prophet's judgment.

The author begins by asserting the duty of all Muslims to follow the Prophet (PBUH), citing the Quranic verse 4:65 to show that faith is incomplete without accepting his authority. He then exposes the hypocrisy of those who claim to seek harmony but turn away from the divine rule. This lesson establishes the foundational principle that Muslims must not mix revelation with other sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and understand the obligation
Focus on the phrase 'الواجب على المسلمين أجمعين اتباع سيد المرسلين' and the overall force of the opening.
The metaphor of the Nile (water for beloved, blood for veiled) sets the tone.
2
Examine the Quranic verse 4:65
Notice that Allah swears by Himself to emphasize the necessity of the Prophet's judgment. This is the strongest proof of the obligation.
The verse is cited to show that faith is not complete without submitting to the Prophet's judgment.
3
Reflect on the hypocrite's claim
The hypocrites claim they only want goodness and harmony, but they turn away from Allah and His Messenger. Recognize the warning against empty claims.
This is a direct link to the groups mentioned in the next lesson.

لك أو عليك)) . (۱) فهو كبحر النيل ماء للمحبوبين ودماء للمحجوبين، فالواجب على المسلمين أجمعين اتباع سيد المرسلين المطابق لما جاء به عقيدة سائر النبيين وعين التبيين للكتاب المبين. وقد بين سبحانه أمره وعظم شأنه وقدره حيث أقسم بنفسه فقال: ﴿ فَلَا وَرَبِّكَ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ حَتَّى أن نحسن يُحكِّمُوكَ فِيمَا شَجَرَ بَيْنَهُمْ ثُمَّ لَا يَجِدُوا فِي أَنْفُسِهِمْ حَرَجًا مِمَّا قَضَيْتَ وَيُسَلِّمُوا تَسْلِيمًا ﴾ [النساء: ٦٥] . وأخبر أن المنافقين يريدون أن يتحاكموا إلى غيره، وأنهم إذا دعوا إلى الله أي كتابه ورسوله أي حكمه صدوا عنه صدودا أي أعرضوا عنه إعراضا مبعودا وأنهم يزعمون أنهم إنما أرادوا إحساناً وتوفيقاً وإيقاناً وتحقيقاً كما يقوله كثير من المتكلمين والمتفلسفة وغيرهم: إنما نريد الأشياء بالجمع بين كلام الأنبياء والحكماء. وكما يقوله كثير من المبتدعة من المتنسكة : إنما نريد الإحسان بالجمع بين الإيمان والإيقان والتوفيق بين الشريعة والطريقة والحقيقة، ويدسون فيها دسائس مذاهبهم الباطلة ومشاربهم العاطلة من الحلول والاتحاد والاتصال والانفصال ودعوى الوجود المطلق وأن الموجودات بأسرها عين الحق ويتوهمون أنهم في مقام الجمعية، والحال أنهم في حال التفرقة وضلال الزندقة. وكما يتفوه كثير من المتملكة والمتأمرة : إنما نريد الإحسان بالسياسة الحسنة البديعة والتوفيق بينهما وبين الشريعة. طلب أن يحكم في شيء من أمر الدين غير ما ثبت عن النبي الأمين صلى الله فكل من عليه وسلم، ويظن أن ذلك مستحسن في باب اليقين، وأن ذلك جامع بين ما جاء به الرسول ما يخالفه من المعقول فله نصيب من ذلك وحرام عليه الترقي إلى ما هنالك، إذ ما جاء به الرسول كاف شاف كامل تبيّن فيه حكم كل حق وباطل قال الله تعالى: وَلَا تَلْبِسُو الْحَقَّ وبين بِالْبَاطِلِ وَتَكْتُبُوا الْحَقَّ وَأَنْتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [البقرة : ٤٢] .
وهذه كانت طريقة السابقين الأولين وهي طريقة التابعين ومن بعدهم من الأئمة المجتهدين وأكابر المفسرين وأعاظم المحدثين وعمدة الصوفية المتقدمين، كداود الطائى والمحاسبي والسري السقطي ومعروف الكرخي والجنيد البغدادى والمتأخرين كأبي نجيب السهروردي وصاحب "عوارف المعارف" والشيخ عبد القادر الجيلاني وأبي القاسم القشيري إلى أن خلف من بعده خلف أضاعوا الصلاة واتبعوا الشهوات وقد آن أن نشرع في المقصود بعون الملك المعبود.
(... for you or against you). So it is like the Nile, water for the beloved and blood for the veiled. So it is obligatory upon all Muslims to follow the master of the messengers, which corresponds to what he brought as the creed of the other prophets and the clear discernment of the manifest Book. He, exalted, clarified his command and magnified his importance and status, for He swore by Himself and said: 'No, by your Lord, they do not believe until they make you judge in what they differ, then they find no discomfort in their hearts from what you decreed and submit fully' [4:65]. And He informed that the hypocrites want to be judged by other than him, and that when they are called to Allah (i.e., His Book) and His Messenger (i.e., His judgment), they turn away in aversion. And they claim that they only intended goodness, harmony, certainty, and verification, as many of the mutakallimun (theologians) and philosophers and others say: 'We only seek things by combining the words of prophets and wise men.' And as many heretics among the ascetics say: 'We only want goodness by combining faith and certainty, and harmony between sharia, tariqa, and haqiqa,' and they insert into it the intrigues of their false doctrines and deleterious tenets, such as hulul (indwelling), ittihad (union), ittisal (connection), infisal (separation), the claim of absolute existence, and that all existents are identical to the Truth. They imagine they are in the station of gathering, while in reality they are in a state of dispersion and the error of zandaqa (heresy). And as many of the kings and rulers declaim: 'We only want goodness by excellent, innovative politics and harmony between them and the sharia.' [They] seek that something of the religious command be judged other than what is established from the trustworthy Prophet, and suppose that is approved in the realm of certainty, and that it combines what the Messenger brought with what contradicts it from reason. So everyone who does that has a share of that, and it is forbidden for him to ascend to that level, for what the Messenger brought is sufficient, healing, and complete, in which the judgment of every truth and falsehood is clarified. Allah said: 'Do not mix truth with falsehood and conceal the truth while you know' [2:42]. And this was the method of the early predecessors, which is the method of the Followers and those after them from the mujtahid imams, the great commentators, the foremost traditionists, and the leading early Sufis, such as Dawud al-Ta'i, al-Muhasibi, al-Sari al-Saqati, Ma'ruf al-Karkhi, al-Junayd al-Baghdadi, and the later ones such as Abu Najib al-Suhrawardi, the author of 'Awarif al-Ma'arif, Shaykh Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, and Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri – until successors came after them who wasted prayer and followed desires. And now it is time that we begin the intended [topic] with the aid of the Possessor of Majesty, the Worshipped.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a condemnation of various groups who attempt to combine the teachings of the Prophet with other sources. The author begins by stating that it is obligatory upon all Muslims to follow the master of the messengers, whose teaching corresponds to the creed of all prophets. He then quotes the Quranic verse (4:65) where Allah swears by Himself that people do not truly believe until they make the Prophet their judge in disputes and submit fully. Next, he mentions that the hypocrites desire to be judged by other than the Prophet and turn away when called to Allah and His messenger. They claim they only intend goodness and harmony. The author then describes three categories of people who make such claims: (1) the mutakallimun and philosophers who claim to combine the words of prophets and wise men; (2) heretical ascetics who claim to integrate sharia, tariqa, and haqiqa, but in fact introduce false doctrines like hulul (indwelling), ittihad (union), and the claim that all existence is identical to God; (3) rulers who aim to combine politics with sharia. All these seek judgments other than what the Prophet established, thinking it is permissible for certainty. The author asserts that what the Prophet brought is sufficient, healing, and complete, clearly distinguishing truth from falsehood, and cites the Quranic verse against mixing truth with falsehood (2:42). He then states that the method of the early predecessors, including the Followers, the great imams, and the early Sufis listed, was different from these innovators. He laments that later generations have lost this path and announces the start of the main subject.

Key Terms
اتباع
المنافقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that following the Prophet is one option among many, and that combining his teachings with other sources is a form of wisdom or harmony.
Correction: The Qur’an declares that true faith requires complete submission to the Prophet’s judgment; anything less is hypocrisy.

Checkpoint
Which Qur’anic verse does the author use to prove that faith requires making the Prophet one’s judge?
A) 2:42
B) 4:65
C) 4:65 is correct
D) 2:102

Key Takeaway
One cannot claim true faith while rejecting the Prophet’s exclusive authority in judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there any area of your life—your marriage, business, or personal choices—where you feel internal discomfort with a ruling of the Prophet? What does that unease reveal about the state of your iman? Will you bring that discomfort before Allah today and ask for a heart that submits fully?
?
You may have sought to harmonize Islamic teachings with modern values, thinking you were pursuing 'goodness, harmony, and certainty' (as the hypocrites claimed). But this verse exposes that such harmonization, if it leads you away from the Prophet's exclusive judgment, is a sign of nifaq. Will you abandon your own reasoning and submit to his decree, even when it clashes with your desires?
?
The Prophet’s judgment is not merely for the big disputes—it applies to every disagreement you face. When you have a conflict with a spouse or a friend, do you genuinely seek the Prophet’s ruling before your own opinion? If not, what is holding you back from making him the ultimate judge? Commit today to one practical step that ensures his judgment comes first.

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
6 min
Three Deceptive Approaches: Combining Revelation with Human Wisdom
The author enumerates three groups that mix revelation with external sources and exposes their errors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main groups that attempt to mix revelation with human wisdom and the specific false doctrines they introduce.

Core Idea
Three groups claim to combine sources, but each introduces falsehood.

In this passage, the author identifies three categories of people who claim to combine the teachings of prophets with other sources: the theologians and philosophers, the heretical ascetics, and the rulers. Each group claims to seek goodness and harmony, but in reality they introduce false beliefs and practices. The author warns against their deception and reaffirms the sufficiency of the Prophet's message.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three groups
The author mentions three groups: mutakallimun/philosophers, heretical ascetics (mubtadi'a), and rulers. Note their distinct claims.
Each group is introduced with 'كما يقوله...'
2
Examine the claim of each group
Theologians and philosophers claim to combine the words of prophets and wise men. Ascetics claim to combine sharia, tariqa, and haqiqa. Rulers claim to combine sharia and politics.
These claims sound positive but are deceptive.
3
Note the specific false doctrines of the ascetics
The ascetics introduce beliefs like hulul (indwelling), ittihad (union), and absolute existence. Recognize these as deviations.
These are classical heresies in Islamic theology.
4
Understand the consequence and proof
The author states that seeking judgment outside the Prophet's teaching is forbidden. He cites verse 2:42 against mixing truth with falsehood.
This verse serves as a general prohibition.

Which false doctrine does the author attribute to the heretical ascetics?
A) Tawhid
B) Hulul and Ittihad
C) Ijtihad

Any attempt to mix revelation with other sources, whether philosophy, mysticism, or politics, is a form of corruption.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself trusting your own reasoning or a 'wise person's' advice over what is clearly established in the Qur'an and Sunnah? How did that feel, and what was the outcome? Will you commit to checking every source against revelation from now on?
?
When you hear people say they want to 'balance' religion with modern life or politics, what is your heart's response? Do you secretly admire that approach, or do you see in it the danger the author exposes? What must you change in your thinking to fully submit to the sufficiency of what the Prophet brought?
?
The author says those who mix truth with falsehood imagine they are in 'the station of gathering' but are actually in 'error of zandaqa.' Are there areas in your life where you have combined a truth from Islam with a falsehood from your own desires or culture, thinking you were being comprehensive? Name one such area right now, and decide: are you willing to separate them, even if it feels less 'balanced'?

beginner

The Path of the Early Predecessors and the Warning Against Innovation
The author praises the methodology of the early Muslim scholars and Sufis as the correct path.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the authentic methodology of the early Muslim scholars and Sufis, and how later generations deviated from it.

Core Idea
The true path is that of the early predecessors, not the innovators who mix sources.

After exposing the errors of those who mix revelation with other sources, the author turns to the positive example of the early Muslims. He lists a chain of righteous predecessors, including the Companions, Followers, imams, commentators, hadith scholars, and early Sufi masters. Their method was pure adherence to revelation without mixing. The author laments that later successors abandoned prayer and followed desires, indicating the need to return to the authentic path.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of early predecessors
Note the categories: Followers, imams, commentators, hadith scholars, early Sufis. The author explicitly names several revered figures.
This list establishes the authoritative chain of transmission.
2
Reflect on the contrast
The early predecessors adhered strictly to revelation, while later generations wasted prayer and followed desires. Understand the decline.
This contrast reinforces the need to return to the original method.
3
Understand the purpose
The author uses this to justify his own work, which aims to clarify the correct creed. The lesson ends with a transition to the main topic.
The author is setting up his own contribution as a continuation of the salaf's method.

(۱) فهو كبحر النيل ماء للمحبوبين ودماء للمحجوبين، فالواجب على المسلمين أجمعين اتباع سيد المرسلين المطابق لما جاء به عقيدة سائر النبيين وعين التبيين للكتاب المبين. وقد بين سبحانه أمره وعظم شأنه وقدره حيث أقسم بنفسه فقال: ﴿ فَلَا وَرَبِّكَ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ حَتَّى أن نحسن يُحكِّمُوكَ فِيمَا شَجَرَ بَيْنَهُمْ ثُمَّ لَا يَجِدُوا فِي أَنْفُسِهِمْ حَرَجًا مِمَّا قَضَيْتَ وَيُسَلِّمُوا تَسْلِيمًا ﴾ [النساء: ٦٥] . وأخبر أن المنافقين يريدون أن يتحاكموا إلى غيره، وأنهم إذا دعوا إلى الله أي كتابه ورسوله أي حكمه صدوا عنه صدودا أي أعرضوا عنه إعراضا مبعودا وأنهم يزعمون أنهم إنما أرادوا إحساناً وتوفيقاً وإيقاناً وتحقيقاً كما يقوله كثير من المتكلمين والمتفلسفة وغيرهم: إنما نريد الأشياء بالجمع بين كلام الأنبياء والحكماء. وكما يقوله كثير من المبتدعة من المتنسكة : إنما نريد الإحسان بالجمع بين الإيمان والإيقان والتوفيق بين الشريعة والطريقة والحقيقة، ويدسون فيها دسائس مذاهبهم الباطلة ومشاربهم العاطلة من الحلول والاتحاد والاتصال والانفصال ودعوى الوجود المطلق وأن الموجودات بأسرها عين الحق ويتوهمون أنهم في مقام الجمعية، والحال أنهم في حال التفرقة وضلال الزندقة. وكما يتفوه كثير من المتملكة والمتأمرة : إنما نريد الإحسان بالسياسة الحسنة البديعة والتوفيق بينهما وبين الشريعة. طلب أن يحكم في شيء من أمر الدين غير ما ثبت عن النبي الأمين صلى الله فكل من عليه وسلم، ويظن أن ذلك مستحسن في باب اليقين، وأن ذلك جامع بين ما جاء به الرسول ما يخالفه من المعقول فله نصيب من ذلك وحرام عليه الترقي إلى ما هنالك، إذ ما جاء به الرسول كاف شاف كامل تبيّن فيه حكم كل حق وباطل قال الله تعالى: وَلَا تَلْبِسُو الْحَقَّ وبين بِالْبَاطِلِ وَتَكْتُبُوا الْحَقَّ وَأَنْتُمْ تَعْلَمُونَ ﴾ [البقرة : ٤٢] .
وهذه كانت طريقة السابقين الأولين وهي طريقة التابعين ومن بعدهم من الأئمة المجتهدين وأكابر المفسرين وأعاظم المحدثين وعمدة الصوفية المتقدمين، كداود الطائى والمحاسبي والسري السقطي ومعروف الكرخي والجنيد البغدادى والمتأخرين كأبي نجيب السهروردي وصاحب "عوارف المعارف" والشيخ عبد القادر الجيلاني وأبي القاسم القشيري إلى أن خلف من بعده خلف أضاعوا الصلاة واتبعوا الشهوات وقد آن أن نشرع في المقصود بعون الملك المعبود.
(... for you or against you). So it is like the Nile, water for the beloved and blood for the veiled. So it is obligatory upon all Muslims to follow the master of the messengers, which corresponds to what he brought as the creed of the other prophets and the clear discernment of the manifest Book. He, exalted, clarified his command and magnified his importance and status, for He swore by Himself and said: 'No, by your Lord, they do not believe until they make you judge in what they differ, then they find no discomfort in their hearts from what you decreed and submit fully' [4:65]. And He informed that the hypocrites want to be judged by other than him, and that when they are called to Allah (i.e., His Book) and His Messenger (i.e., His judgment), they turn away in aversion. And they claim that they only intended goodness, harmony, certainty, and verification, as many of the mutakallimun (theologians) and philosophers and others say: 'We only seek things by combining the words of prophets and wise men.' And as many heretics among the ascetics say: 'We only want goodness by combining faith and certainty, and harmony between sharia, tariqa, and haqiqa,' and they insert into it the intrigues of their false doctrines and deleterious tenets, such as hulul (indwelling), ittihad (union), ittisal (connection), infisal (separation), the claim of absolute existence, and that all existents are identical to the Truth. They imagine they are in the station of gathering, while in reality they are in a state of dispersion and the error of zandaqa (heresy). And as many of the kings and rulers declaim: 'We only want goodness by excellent, innovative politics and harmony between them and the sharia.' [They] seek that something of the religious command be judged other than what is established from the trustworthy Prophet, and suppose that is approved in the realm of certainty, and that it combines what the Messenger brought with what contradicts it from reason. So everyone who does that has a share of that, and it is forbidden for him to ascend to that level, for what the Messenger brought is sufficient, healing, and complete, in which the judgment of every truth and falsehood is clarified. Allah said: 'Do not mix truth with falsehood and conceal the truth while you know' [2:42]. And this was the method of the early predecessors, which is the method of the Followers and those after them from the mujtahid imams, the great commentators, the foremost traditionists, and the leading early Sufis, such as Dawud al-Ta'i, al-Muhasibi, al-Sari al-Saqati, Ma'ruf al-Karkhi, al-Junayd al-Baghdadi, and the later ones such as Abu Najib al-Suhrawardi, the author of 'Awarif al-Ma'arif, Shaykh Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, and Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri – until successors came after them who wasted prayer and followed desires. And now it is time that we begin the intended [topic] with the aid of the Possessor of Majesty, the Worshipped.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a condemnation of various groups who attempt to combine the teachings of the Prophet with other sources. The author begins by stating that it is obligatory upon all Muslims to follow the master of the messengers, whose teaching corresponds to the creed of all prophets. He then quotes the Quranic verse (4:65) where Allah swears by Himself that people do not truly believe until they make the Prophet their judge in disputes and submit fully. Next, he mentions that the hypocrites desire to be judged by other than the Prophet and turn away when called to Allah and His messenger. They claim they only intend goodness and harmony. The author then describes three categories of people who make such claims: (1) the mutakallimun and philosophers who claim to combine the words of prophets and wise men; (2) heretical ascetics who claim to integrate sharia, tariqa, and haqiqa, but in fact introduce false doctrines like hulul (indwelling), ittihad (union), and the claim that all existence is identical to God; (3) rulers who aim to combine politics with sharia. All these seek judgments other than what the Prophet established, thinking it is permissible for certainty. The author asserts that what the Prophet brought is sufficient, healing, and complete, clearly distinguishing truth from falsehood, and cites the Quranic verse against mixing truth with falsehood (2:42). He then states that the method of the early predecessors, including the Followers, the great imams, and the early Sufis listed, was different from these innovators. He laments that later generations have lost this path and announces the start of the main subject.

التابعين
الأئمة المجتهدين
الصوفية المتقدمين

Key Takeaway
The correct method is to follow the early predecessors in pure adherence to revelation, not to mix sources.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly examine your spiritual practices to see if they align with the path of the early predecessors, or do you follow practices because they are popular or comforting? What specific practice in your life might be closer to the 'wasted prayer' that the author warns about? Commit to checking one thing today.
?
The author lists many renowned scholars and Sufis as examples of the true path. Are any of your religious figures or teachers you look up to similar to those mentioned? Hold yourself accountable: does your influence from them lead you to pure adherence to revelation, or to mixing? Write down one way you can purify your following.
?
The early predecessors are described as those who did not mix sources. Where in your own life have you mixed the sources of revelation with personal opinion or cultural practice? This week, identify one area and discard the mixed element.

The Stance Against Tashbih and the Slander of the Jahmiyyah
Two Salaf quotes and a response to Jahmiyya slander

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the balanced Sunni position against both tashbih and ta'til, and how the Jahmiyya slander Ahl al-Sunna while being the true deniers of God's attributes.

Core Idea
Affirming Allah's attributes without likeness is the middle path between tashbih and ta'til.

This passage from the commentary of al-Qunawi presents two key statements from Salaf scholars that define the Sunni stance: one must neither liken Allah to creation nor deny His self-described attributes. The author then exposes the deceptive tactic of the Jahmiyya who label Ahl al-Sunna as anthropomorphists, while they themselves are the ones who empty God of His attributes. Let's read the source to see how this argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the statements of Nu'aym ibn Hammad and Ishaq ibn Rahwayh
Carefully read their rulings on tashbih and ta'til. Notice that they condemn both extremes equally.
Both scholars are early Salaf authorities.
2
Identify the accusation of the Jahmiyya
Find where the author mentions that Jahm and his followers claim Ahl al-Sunna are mushabbiha. Understand their tactic.
3
Recognize who the real mu'attila are
The passage states that the Jahmiyya themselves are the mu'attila (deniers of attributes). Note how this flips the accusation.
4
Learn the sign of the Jahmiyya from the Salaf
Many Salaf imams said that calling Ahl al-Sunna 'mushabbiha' is a sign of the Jahmiyya. Reflect on why this is a consistent pattern.
5
Consider the examples given
The passage mentions that even some Mu'tazila commentators like Abd al-Jabbar and Zamakhshari use this slander. Think about the broader context.
The passage ends mid-sentence but the point is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في شرح القونوي" قال نعيم بن حماد: من شبه الله بشيء من خلقه فقد كفر ومن أنكر ما وصف الله به نفسه فقد كفر. وقال إسحاق ابن راهويه من وصف الله فشبه صفاته بصفات من خلق الله فهو كافر بالله العظيم. وقال: علامه جهم وأصحابه دعواهم على أهل السنة والجماعة وما أولعوا به من الكذب أنهم مشبهة بل هم المعطلة، ولذا قال كثير من أئمة السلف: علامة الجهمية تسميتهم أهل السنة مشبهة، فإنه ما من أحد شيء من الأسماء والصفات إلا يسمي من نفاة المثبت لها مشبها حتى بعض المفسرين كعبد الجبار والزمخشري وغيرهما من
In the commentary of al-Qūnawī: Nuʿaym ibn Ḥammād said: 'Whoever likens Allah to anything from His creation has disbelieved, and whoever denies what Allah has described Himself with has disbelieved.' And Isḥāq ibn Rāhwayh said: 'Whoever describes Allah and likens His attributes to the attributes of His creation is an unbeliever in Allah, the Mighty.' And he said: 'The hallmark of Jahm and his companions is their claim against Ahl al-Sunna wa-l-Jamāʿa and their obsession with falsehood that they are anthropomorphists (mushabbiha), but rather they (the Jahmiyya) are the deniers (al-muʿaṭṭila). Therefore many of the Salaf imams said: The sign of the Jahmiyya is that they call Ahl al-Sunna 'mushabbiha'. For no one is there from the negators of the names and attributes but that they call the affirmers of them 'mushabbih', even some commentators like ʿAbd al-Jabbār and al-Zamakhsharī and others from...
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents the position against tashbih (anthropomorphism) from the Salaf. It begins with a citation from the commentary of al-Qūnawī, quoting Nuʿaym ibn Ḥammād and Isḥāq ibn Rāhwayh. Both denounce tashbih as kufr, but also affirm that denying what Allah has described Himself with is equally kufr. This establishes a balanced approach: neither likening Allah to creation nor stripping Him of His attributes. The author then points out that Jahm and his followers (the Jahmiyya) slander Ahl al-Sunna by calling them 'mushabbiha', but in reality the Jahmiyya are the 'muʿaṭṭila' (those who empty Allah of His attributes). The author identifies this as a sign of the Jahmiyya. The passage notes that this tactic is employed even by some renowned commentators like ʿAbd al-Jabbār and al-Zamakhsharī, who are from the Muʿtazila.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming Allah's attributes means comparing Him to creation.
Correction: The Salaf affirms attributes without likeness; both tashbih and ta'til are kufr.

Checkpoint

A) He is a sinner but not a disbeliever
B) He has disbelieved
C) He is excused due to ignorance
D) He is a believer if he intends good

Key Takeaway
The Salaf maintained a balanced position: rejection of both tashbih and ta'til, and they exposed the Jahmiyya's slander as a hallmark of their deviation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses like 'the hand of Allah is above their hands' or 'the Most Merciful established upon the Throne', do you feel a discomfort that tempts you to twist the meaning into something else? Which extreme do you drift toward—denial or imagination—and what verse will you memorize to anchor yourself in the Salaf's path of affirmation without likeness?
?
The Jahmiyya slandered the most pious of this ummah as anthropomorphists. Reflect: In your heart, have you ever looked down on a simple believer who affirms Allah's attributes literally, thinking they are naive or crude? That is the same seed of arrogance that led the Jahmiyya to label the Salaf. Repent and ask Allah to purify your heart from such contempt.
?
You are not a Jahmi, but you live in an age flooded with rationalism that subtly denies Allah's attributes. When a scholar says 'Allah has a hand but we don't know how', do you inwardly accept it or feel pressure to explain it away? Commit today to say 'I affirm it as the Salaf did' and then stop—no further, no less.

Refuting the Mu'tazila on the Createdness of the Qur'an
Refutation of Mu'tazila argument and explanation of their alternative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila's argument that the Qur'an's created qualities prove its speech is created only refutes the Hanabila position, not the orthodox Sunni position.

Core Idea
The physical composition of the Qur'an is created, but the eternal speech is the meaning in God.

The Mu'tazila argue that because the Qur'an has qualities like composition and revelation, it must be created. The author responds that this argument only works against those who believe the letters are eternal. The orthodox view holds that the composition is created, while the eternal speech is the meaning (kalam nafsi). Then he explains the Mu'tazila's own alternative interpretation of God's speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the overall flow.
The passage is dense; read carefully.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila argument
Find the list of qualities they claim prove the Qur'an is created.
These include composition, ordering, revelation, being Arabic, etc.
3
Understand the refutation
Note why the author says this only refutes the Hanabila, not the orthodox Sunni position.
Because the orthodox hold that the composition (nazm) is created, but the eternal speech is the meaning.
4
Examine the Mu'tazila alternative
See how the Mu'tazila interpret God being Mutakallim: as originator of sounds and letters in some substrate.
This avoids affirming an eternal attribute of speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما استدلالهم بأن القرآن متصف بما هو من صفات المخلوق، وسمات الحدوث من التأليف والتنظيم والنزول والتنزيل وكونه عربياً مسموعاً فصيحاً معجزاً إلى غير ذلك، فإنما يقوم حجة على الحنابلة لا علينا؛ لأنا قائلون بحدوث النظم أيضاً، وإنما الكلام في معنى القديم، والمعتزلة لما لم يمكنهم إنكار كونه متكلما ذهبوا إلى أنه متكلم بمعنى موجد الأصوات والحروف في محالها وأشكال الكتابة في اللوح المحفوظ وإن لم يقرأ على اختلاف قامت به الحركة لا من أوجدها.
As for their argument that the Qur'an is described with attributes of the created and marks of originatedness, such as composition, ordering, descending, revelation, being Arabic, audible, eloquent, miraculous, etc., it only constitutes a proof against the Hanabila, not against us; for we also hold that the composition (al-nazm) is originated. The discussion is only concerning the meaning of the eternal. The Mu'tazila, since they could not deny that He is Mutakallim, went to [saying] that He is Mutakallim in the sense of the originator of sounds and letters in their loci and shapes of writing in the Preserved Tablet, even if it is not recited, according to a difference... [the movement subsists in it?] not the one who originated it.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a response to the Mu'tazila's argument. They claimed the Qur'an must be created because it has characteristics of created things (composition, ordering, revelation, being Arabic, etc.). The author replies that this is only a valid argument against the Hanabila (anthropomorphists) who believe the literal words and letters are eternal. The orthodox position agrees that the physical composition (nazm) is created; the real eternal speech is the meaning subsisting in God. Then he explains the Mu'tazila's alternative: since they cannot deny God is Mutakallim, they interpret it as God creating sounds and letters in some substrate (like the angel or the Preserved Tablet). This reduces speech to an act of creation, not an attribute.

Key Terms
الحنابلة
النظم
موجد الأصوات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The orthodox Sunni position believes the Arabic Qur'an (words and letters) is eternal.
Correction: The orthodox position holds that only the meaning (kalam nafsi) is eternal; the physical composition (nazm) is created.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's argument that the Qur'an's created qualities prove its creation only refutes those who deny creation of the composition; the orthodox hold that the composition is created and the eternal speech is the meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Qur'an, do you truly sense that you are engaging with something that originates from God's eternal speech, or do you unconsciously treat it as a mere human-like composition? What would change in your recitation if you internalized that the words are created but the meaning is from God?
?
The Mu'tazila redefined God's speech to avoid affirming an eternal attribute. Are there any attributes of God that you unintentionally redefined or minimized in your mind to make Him more 'comprehensible'? Commit to reflecting on one specific attribute this week and ask yourself whether you are truly accepting it as God describes it.
?
If the composition of the Qur'an is created, then every letter and sound you hear is a created thing that points to the uncreated. When you listen to the Qur'an, do you pause at the veil of creation to contemplate the eternal meaning behind it, or do you stop at the surface? Challenge yourself: before your next recitation, consciously remind yourself that the meaning is from God and let that awe reshape your heart.

Refuting the Claim about Ibn Arabi and Pharaoh's Faith
Refutation of the attribution to Ibn Arabi of belief in Pharaoh's faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that Ibn Arabi believed in Pharaoh's faith is false, and see the evidence refuting it from his own works and later scholars.

Core Idea
Ibn Arabi clearly stated Pharaoh is in Hell forever; the claim otherwise is slander.

This passage defends the orthodoxy of the great Sufi master Ibn Arabi against a serious accusation: that he believed the Pharaoh of Moses died with faith. The author provides multiple proofs—from Ibn Arabi's own ambiguous style meant for the elite, a direct quotation from his magnum opus al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya saying Pharaoh is eternally damned, and the testimony of later scholars who held him in high esteem. Let us examine these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim being refuted
Read the Arabic passage once and note that it begins by refuting someone named Ibn al-Arabi (or Ibn Arabi). Understand that the core accusation is that Ibn Arabi believed Pharaoh had faith.
The passage later clarifies this is a slander.
2
Notice the explanation of Ibn Arabi's intentionally ambiguous language
The author explains that Ibn Arabi used ambiguous language so that only the elite would understand his deeper meanings. This is illustrated by a poetic couplet from al-Futuhat.
This shows that his words should not be taken at face value by those unfamiliar with his style.
3
Focus on al-Sharani's direct quote from Ibn Arabi's al-Futuhat
Imam al-Sharani explicitly states that Ibn Arabi wrote in Chapter 62 that Pharaoh is from the people of Hell and will never leave. This is the clearest refutation.
Al-Futuhat is among Ibn Arabi's later works, so it represents his final view.
4
Consider the titles given to Ibn Arabi by Ahmad Rida Khan
The passage lists many honorific titles bestowed upon Ibn Arabi, indicating his high status and orthodoxy in the eyes of later scholars.
This reinforces that the accusation contradicts the consensus of the Ahl al-Sunna.

Source Text

وهو أبو بكر محمد بن عبد الله. (۲) وهي فر العون من القول وفيه رد على ابن العربي (٢) ومن تبعه كالجلال الدواني وقد ألفت رسالة مستقلة في تحقيق هذه المسألة وبينت ما وقع لهم من الوهم في المواضع المشكلة وأتيت بوضوح الأدلة المستجمعة من الكتاب والسنة ونصوص الأئمة. بقوله: اعتمد ابن عربي في كتابة مؤلفاته على لغة مبهمة عن قصد ؛ لكي يفهم الأهل فقط، وسئل مرة عما يعنيه فأجاب من فوره يا من يراني ولا أراه كم ذا أراه ولا يراني يا من يراني مجرما ولا أراه آخذا كم ذا أراه منعما ولا يراني لائذا (الفتوحات المكية، الباب السابع والمأتان في حال العلة، ٢١٧/٤) قال الإمام عبد الوهاب الشعراني قدس سره الرباني: ومن دعوى المنكر أن الشيخ يقول بقبول إيمان فرعون وذلك كذب وافتراء على الشيخ فقد صرح الشيخ في الباب الثاني والستين من "الفتوحات" بأن فرعون من أهل النار الذين لا يخرجون منها أبد الآبدين و"الفتوحات" من أواخر مؤلفاته فإنه فرغ منها قبل موته بنحو ثلاث سنين . اليواقيت والجواهر، ص: ۱۷) ولقد لقب الأمام أحمد رضا خان عليه رحمة الرحمن الشيخ رضا خان عليه رحمة الرحمن الشيخ الأكبر ابن عربي بألقاب كثيرة ومنها: (۱) حضرت سيدي امام المکاشفين محی اللہ والدين شیخ اکبر ابن عربی (۲) امام اجل، عارف كبير (۳) امام الطريقة بحر الحقيقة سیدنا شیخ اکبر محی الدین ابن عربی رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ فتوحات مکیہ شریف میں فرماتے ہیں ( ٤ ) حضرت خاتم الولایۃ المحمدیة فی زمانہ بحر الحقائق ولسان القوم بجنانه و بيانه سيدي شیخ اکبر محی الدین ابن عربي نَفَعَنَا اللَّهُ فِي الدَّارَين بفيضانه.
And he is Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abdullah. (2) It is the release of help from the statement, and in it is a refutation of Ibn al-Arabi (2) and those who follow him like al-Jalal al-Dawani, and I have authored an independent treatise on the investigation of this issue and explained the error that befell them in the problematic places, and I brought clear evidence gathered from the Book, the Sunna, and the texts of the Imams. By his saying: Ibn Arabi relied in writing his works on intentionally ambiguous language so that only the people of understanding would understand. He was once asked what he meant, and he immediately replied: 'O you who see me and I do not see you, how often I see you and you do not see me. O you who see me as a sinner and I do not see you taking, how often I see you as a benefactor and you do not see me seeking refuge.' (al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya, Chapter 207, on the state of illness, 4/217). Imam Abd al-Wahhab al-Sharani, may his secret be sanctified, said: 'Among the false claims of the deniers is that the Shaykh says that the faith of Pharaoh is accepted, and that is a lie and slander against the Shaykh. For the Shaykh clearly stated in Chapter 62 of al-Futuhat that Pharaoh is among the people of the Fire who will never leave it forever. And al-Futuhat is among his later works, for he completed it about three years before his death.' (al-Yawaqit wa al-Jawahir, p. 17). And Imam Ahmad Rida Khan, may the mercy of the All-Merciful be upon him, gave the Greatest Shaykh Ibn Arabi many titles, among them: (1) Hadrat Sayyidi Imam al-Mukashifin Muhyi Allah wa al-Din Shaykh Akbar Ibn Arabi, (2) Imam Ajall, Arif Kabir, (3) Imam al-Tariqa, Bahr al-Haqiqa, Sayyiduna Shaykh Akbar Muhyi al-Din Ibn Arabi, may Allah be pleased with him. In al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya he says: (4) Hadrat Khatam al-Wilaya al-Muhammadiyya fi Zamanihi, Bahr al-Haqa'iq wa Lisan al-Qaum bi Jinanihi wa Bayanihi, Sayyidi Shaykh Akbar Muhyi al-Din Ibn Arabi, may Allah benefit us in both abodes through his overflow.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that Ibn Arabi held that Pharaoh died with faith. The author first identifies that this work contains a refutation of Ibn Arabi and those who follow him, and mentions that he has written a separate treatise on this issue. Then he provides evidence from Ibn Arabi's own words, citing a poetic reply that shows his ambiguous style but does not indicate any heretical belief. Next, he quotes al-Sharani who explicitly says that Ibn Arabi stated in al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya that Pharaoh is forever in Hell, thus refuting the allegation. Finally, he cites the titles given to Ibn Arabi by Ahmad Rida Khan, showing his high regard and orthodoxy. The passage defends Ibn Arabi's orthodoxy and warns against slander.

Key Terms
ابن عربي
إيمان فرعون
الفتوحات المكية
الشعراني
أحمد رضا خان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ibn Arabi believed that Pharaoh had faith and will be saved.
Correction: Ibn Arabi explicitly stated in al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya that Pharaoh is from the people of the Fire and will never leave Hell.

Checkpoint
According to al-Sharani, what did Ibn Arabi say about Pharaoh in al-Futuhat?
A) Pharaoh had faith and will be saved
B) Pharaoh is in Hell forever
C) Pharaoh's fate is unknown
D) Pharaoh is in al-Barzakh

Key Takeaway
Ibn Arabi definitively stated that Pharaoh is in Hell forever; any claim otherwise is a slander against him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time you heard a negative claim about a scholar or a Muslim figure. Did you investigate it yourself before forming an opinion? Will you commit to always checking the original source before passing on such claims?
?
Ibn Arabi used ambiguous language to protect deeper meanings. Are there times when you have simplified or misrepresented someone's words to fit your narrative? How can you ensure you convey others' statements accurately, especially in matters of faith?
?
The author says Ibn Arabi clearly stated Pharaoh is in Hell, yet slander persists. Are you carrying any unfounded beliefs about scholars or about people that you haven't verified? What step will you take today to correct it?

Obligation of Good Opinion toward Awliya
Al-Nawawi and al-Sha'rani establish the ruling on good opinion of awliya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic obligation to hold a good opinion of the awliya (saints) and to interpret their statements and actions in the best possible light.

Core Idea
Thinking ill of awliya is forbidden; interpreting them well is a duty for every rational person.

This lesson presents a key principle from the classical tradition: that Muslims must avoid negative assumptions about the awliya (friends of Allah). It quotes the great scholar al-Nawawi and the renowned mystic al-Sha'rani to establish that one must always interpret the words and deeds of awliya favorably, unless one has reached their station. This principle protects the respect due to the righteous and prevents slander.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Notice how al-Nawawi and al-Sha'rani articulate the ruling.
The passage begins with al-Nawawi's response about Ibn 'Arabi.
2
Understand the ruling
Identify the two key legal rulings: it is forbidden to think ill of awliya, and it is obligatory to interpret their words and actions favorably.
The obligation of ta'wil is emphasized.
3
Note the limitation
The ruling applies to those who have not reached the station of the awliya. Those who have attained their rank may have a different perspective.
Only those with 'little success' fail to do this.
4
Reflect on the principle
Consider why this principle is important for maintaining respect and unity among Muslims, especially regarding revered figures.

وإن كان صحيحا فالعبارات مصروفة عن الظاهر فسئل الإمام محي الدين النووي عن الشيخ محي عربي فقال تلك أمة قد خلت، ولكن الذي عندنا أنه يحرم على كل عاقل أن يسيء الظن بأحد من أولياء : الله عز وجل ويجب عليه أن يؤول أقوالهم وأفعالهم ما دام لم يلحق بدرجتهم ولا يعجز عن ذلك إلا قليل التوفيق. اليواقيت والجواهر للشعراني، ص: ۱۲) يا من يراني ولا أراه كم ذا أراه ولا يراني يا من يراني مجرما ولا أراه كم ذا أراه منعما ولا يراني لائذا قال الإمام عبد الوهاب الشعراني قدس سره الرباني: ومن دعوى المنكر أن الشيخ يقول بقبول إيمان فرعون وذلك كذب وافتراء على الشيخ فقد صرح الشيخ في الباب الثاني والستين من "الفتوحات" بأن فرعون من أهل النار الذين لا يخرجون منها أبد الآبدين و"الفتوحات" من أواخر مؤلفاته فإنه فرغ منها قبل موته بنحو ثلاث سنين . اليواقيت والجواهر، ص: ۱۷) ولقد لقب الأمام أحمد رضا خان عليه رحمة الرحمن الشيخ رضا خان عليه رحمة الرحمن الشيخ الأكبر ابن عربي بألقاب كثيرة ومنها: (۱) حضرت سیدی امام المکاشفین محی اللہ والدین شیخ اکبر ابن عربی (۲) امام اجل، عارف كبير (۳) امام الطريقة بحر الحقيقة سیدنا شیخ اکبر محی الدین ابن عربی رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ فتوحات مکیہ شریف میں فرماتے ہیں ( ٤ ) حضرت خاتم الولایۃ المحمدیة فی زمانہ بحر الحقائق ولسان القوم بجنانه و بيانه سيدي شيخ اكبر محي الدين ابن عربي نَفَعَنَا اللَّهُ فِي الدَّارَين بفيضانه.
And if it is true, then the expressions are turned away from the literal meaning. So al-Imam Muhyi al-Din al-Nawawi was asked about al-Shaykh Muhyi al-Din Ibn 'Arabi, and he said: 'Those are a nation that has passed away.' But what we have is that it is forbidden for every rational person to think ill of any of the awliya of Allah, and it is obligatory to interpret their words and actions as long as one has not reached their station, and only those with little success are incapable of that. (from al-Yawaqit wa al-Jawahir by al-Sha'rani, p. 12). 'O He who sees me and I do not see Him, how often do I see Him and He does not see me? Indeed, the Shaykh stated in chapter sixty-two of al-Futuhat that Pharaoh is among the people of the Fire who will never leave it. And al-Futuhat is among his later works, for he completed it about three years before his death. (al-Yawaqit wa al-Jawahir, p. 17). And indeed, al-Imam Ahmad Rida Khan, may mercy of the Merciful be upon him, gave the Shaykh al-Akbar Ibn 'Arabi many titles, including: (1) hadrat sayyidi imam al-mukashifin muhyi allah wa al-din shaykh akbar ibn arabi, (2) imam ajall, arif kabir, (3) imam al-tariqa bahr al-haqiqa sayyiduna shaykh akbar muhy al-din ibn arabi radiya allahu ta'ala anhu, in al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya sharif he says: (4) hadrat khatam al-wilaya al-muhammadiyya fi zamanihi bahr al-haqa'iq wa lisan al-qawm bijinanihi wa bayanihi sayyidi shaykh akbar muhy al-din ibn arabi nafa'ana allahu fi al-darayn bifaydanih.

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Ibn 'Arabi against his critics. It begins by citing Imam al-Nawawi's response that we should not speak ill of past scholars, and that it is obligatory to interpret the words of awliya favorably. Then it includes a poetic line by Ibn 'Arabi expressing his humility before God. Next, al-Sha'rani refutes the accusation that Ibn 'Arabi believed in the acceptance of Pharaoh's faith, citing Ibn 'Arabi's own words from al-Futuhat that Pharaoh is in Hell forever. Finally, it lists the honorific titles given to Ibn 'Arabi by later scholars, showing his high status. The overall goal is to defend Ibn 'Arabi's orthodoxy and to instruct the reader to avoid thinking ill of awliya.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is acceptable to criticize awliya if they say something seemingly unorthodox.
Correction: The passage teaches that it is forbidden to think ill of awliya and obligatory to interpret their words favorably, as long as one has not reached their station.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on thinking ill of awliya?
A) Recommended to avoid but not required.
B) Forbidden for every rational person.
C) Permissible if there is evidence.
D) Required to show respect.

Key Takeaway
Good opinion of awliya is obligatory; interpreting their words favorably is a duty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself thinking negatively about a pious person because of something they said or did? What would it cost you to now replace that thought with a favorable interpretation, as this lesson commands? Will you do it today?
?
The lesson says that only those with little divine success fail to interpret the words of awliya in the best way. How does this truth challenge your own habit of judging others? Are you ready to ask Allah for tawfiq to change that, starting with a specific person you have judged?
?
Think of a time when you criticized a righteous person. Can you honestly find a possible favorable interpretation for their action now? If you cannot, does your inability expose a lack of tawfiq in your own heart? What repentance or change does this demand from you?

Defense of Ibn 'Arabi: Refuting the Pharaoh Accusation
Refutation of the Pharaoh accusation and enumeration of Ibn 'Arabi's honorary titles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two key defenses of Ibn 'Arabi: the refutation of the false claim that he accepted Pharaoh's faith, and the high regard in which later scholars held him.

Core Idea
Ibn 'Arabi was a great wali, and false accusations against him, like the Pharaoh claim, are baseless.

This lesson continues the defense of Ibn 'Arabi. It includes a humble verse from Ibn 'Arabi himself, then a direct refutation by al-Sha'rani of the notorious accusation that Ibn 'Arabi believed Pharaoh's faith would be accepted. Finally, it lists the many honorary titles given to him by later scholars, including Ahmad Rida Khan, showing his esteemed position in the Sufi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the poetic verse by Ibn 'Arabi
Read the Arabic verse and its translation. Notice the tone of humility and awe before God.
This verse is attributed to Ibn 'Arabi.
2
Understand the Pharaoh accusation
Realize that some people claimed Ibn 'Arabi taught that Pharaoh's faith (iman) was accepted. This is the accusation being refuted.
The claim is called a lie and slander.
3
Study al-Sha'rani's refutation
Al-Sha'rani quotes Ibn 'Arabi's own words from al-Futuhat al-Makkiyya, stating that Pharaoh is among the people of Hell forever.
Al-Futuhat is one of Ibn 'Arabi's later works.
4
Read the list of honorific titles
Notice the variety of titles given to Ibn 'Arabi by Ahmad Rida Khan, indicating his high spiritual rank.
Titles include 'imam al-mukashifin' and 'khatam al-wilaya'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a negative accusation against a scholar of the past, do you immediately accept it or do you seek the scholar's own works to verify? This passage shows how al-Sha'rani directly quoted Ibn 'Arabi's writing to refute a false claim. Are you willing to do the same when you hear rumors about your teachers or the righteous? What steps will you take to verify before spreading such claims?
?
The passage begins with Ibn 'Arabi's own words of profound humility before Allah: 'O He who sees me as a sinner and I do not see Him, how often do I see Him as a bestower of blessings and He does not see me as one seeking refuge.' Despite his high station as the 'seal of sainthood', he saw himself as a sinner. How does your own spiritual pride compare? When was the last time you felt truly humble before Allah, acknowledging your sins while recognizing His blessings? Write a personal dua inspired by this poetic expression.
?
Consider the honorific titles given to Ibn 'Arabi: imam of unveilers, seal of Muhammadan sainthood. If you were to be remembered, what titles would people give you based on your actual life? Are you living in a way that deserves such remembrance? What needs to change so that your reality matches the honor you desire?

Understanding Takfir: Ingratitude vs. Apostasy
The author interprets rulings on takfir regarding the createdness of the Quran, distinguishing between ingratitude and apostasy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between kufr of ingratitude and apostasy in the context of the createdness of the Quran, and how this applies to Imam Abu Hanifa's statements.

Core Idea
The takfir for saying the Quran is created is kufr of ingratitude, not apostasy, except for the Mu'tazila.

This lesson clarifies a crucial distinction in Islamic theology regarding the charge of disbelief (takfir). Certain statements from Imam Abu Hanifa and other scholars about those who say the Quran is created could be misunderstood. The author explains that such rulings refer to a less severe form of disbelief—ingratitude for blessings—rather than outright apostasy, with a specific exception for the Mu'tazila sect. Understanding this nuance prevents hasty judgments and preserves communal unity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic text and its literal English translation to grasp the author's exact words.
Pay attention to the key terms in Arabic.
2
Identify key terms
Note the terms: takfir, kufran al-ni‘ma, kufr al-khuruj min al-milla, and Mu'tazila. These are central to the argument.
3
Understand the distinction
The author distinguishes two types of kufr: ingratitude (kufran al-ni‘ma) and apostasy (kufr al-khuruj). The takfir reported from Imam Abu Hanifa is of the first type, except for the Mu'tazila.
Consider why the Mu'tazila are exempted from this leniency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن ما جاء في كلام الإمام الأعظم وغيره من علماء الأنام من تكفير القائل بخلق القرآن فمحمول على كفران النعمة لا كفر الخروج من الملة، بخلاف المعتزلة في هذه المسألة،
And know that what has come in the speech of the Great Imam (Abu Hanifa) and others of the scholars of mankind regarding declaring the one who says the Quran is created to be a disbeliever is interpreted as ingratitude for blessings (kufran al-ni‘ma), not as apostasy (kufr al-khuruj min al-milla), contrary to the Mu‘tazila in this matter.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage addresses a sensitive issue: some statements from Imam Abu Hanifa and other scholars declared those who say the Quran is created to be disbelievers (kafir). The author clarifies that this ruling is to be understood as 'kufr of ingratitude' (kufran al-ni‘ma) — i.e., a severe sin but not necessarily apostasy that removes one from the Islamic community. However, the exception is the Mu'tazila, who famously held that the Quran is created; their position is treated differently (presumably as actual apostasy) because they made it a central tenet. The passage thus protects the status of Muslims who might fall into error out of ignorance while firmly opposing the Mu'tazilite doctrine.

Key Terms
تكفير
خلق القرآن
كفران النعمة
كفر الخروج من الملة
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that Imam Abu Hanifa considered every person who says the Quran is created to be an apostate.
Correction: The passage clarifies that his ruling is kufr of ingratitude, not apostasy, except for the Mu'tazila.

Checkpoint
How does the author interpret the takfir of those who say the Quran is created, as reported from Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) As apostasy.
B) As a type of disbelief in Allah.
C) As ingratitude for blessings (kufran al-ni‘ma).
D) As a metaphorical expression.

Key Takeaway
The takfir attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the createdness of the Quran is a less severe form of disbelief—ingratitude—not apostasy, except for the Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a Muslim who holds a questionable belief, do you tend to write them off entirely? How can the distinction between kufran al-ni‘ma and apostasy change your attitude toward them?
?
Are there blessings in your life for which you fail to show gratitude, effectively committing kufran al-ni‘ma? What one step will you take today to turn ingratitude into thankfulness?
?
Imagine someone sincerely ignorant of a doctrine says something mistaken. Would you label them as outside Islam? How does this lesson press you to be more cautious in your judgments?

Three Early Schools on Divine Speech
Commentator lists the first three of nine schools on divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first three historical positions on the nature of divine speech: the Sabian-philosopher view of emanation, the Mu'tazilite view of creation, and the Kullabi-Ash'ari view of a single eternal meaning.

Core Idea
Divine speech: emanation, creation, or eternal meaning?

The commentator begins by listing nine schools of thought on divine speech. This lesson covers the first three, which represent the earliest major positions. By understanding these, you will see how later views built upon or reacted to them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Note how each view is introduced with 'أحدها', 'ثانيها', 'ثالثها'.
The terms 'الصابئة' and 'المعتزلة' are key.
2
Identify each school's core claim
For each of the three views, identify what they say about the nature of divine speech: is it an emanation, a creation, or an eternal meaning?
3
Consider the implications
Think about what each view implies about God's relationship to scripture. Does scripture become temporal or eternal?
This sets the stage for later kalam debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال شارحه قد افترق الناس في مسألة الكلام على تسعة أقوال: أحدها: أن كلام الله تعالى هو ما يفيض على النفوس من المعاني، إما من العقل الفعال عند بعضهم أو من غيره، وهذا قول الصابئة والمتفلسفة. وثانيها: أنه مخلوق خلقه الله منفصلا عنه، وهذا قول المعتزلة. وثالثها: أنه معنى واحد قائم بذات الله هو الأمر والنهي والخبر والاستخبار، إن عبّر عنه بالعربية كان قرآنا، وإن عبّر عنه بالعبرية كان توراة، وهذا قول ابن كلاب ومن وافقه كالأشعري وغيره. ورابعها أنه حروف وأصوات أزلية مجتمعة في الأزل، وهذا قول طائفة من أهل الكلام والحديث. وخامسها أنه حروف وأصوات لكن تكلم الله بها بعد أن لم يكن متكلما، وهذا قول الكرامية وغيرهم. وسادسها أن كلامه يرجع إلى ما يحدثه علمه وإرادته القائم بذاته، وهذا يقوله صاحب المعتبر و يميل إليه الرازي في المطالب العالية. وسابعها: أن كلامه يتضمن معنى قائما بذاته هو ما خلقه في غيره وهذا قول أبي منصور الماتريدي. وثامنها : أنه مشترك بين المعنى القديم القائم بالذات وبين ما يخلقه في غيره من الأصوات، وهذا قول أبي المعالي ومن تبعه قلت والأظهر أن المعنى الأول حقيقة. والثاني مجاز. وتاسعها أنه تعالى لم يزل متكلما إذا شاء ومتى شاء وكيف شاء وهو يتكلم به بصوت يسمع، وإن نوع الكلام قديم وإن لم يكن الصوت المعين قديما قلت: وهذا يؤيده ما قدمناه وهو المأثور عن أئمة الحديث والسنة.
And its commentator said: People have differed on the issue of speech into nine statements: The first: that the speech of Allah the Exalted is what overflows upon souls of meanings, either from the Active Intellect according to some, or from other than it, and this is the statement of the Sabians and the philosophers. The second: that it is a creation which Allah created separate from Him, and this is the statement of the Mu'tazila. The third: that it is one meaning subsisting in Allah's essence, which is command, prohibition, news, and interrogation; if expressed in Arabic it is the Quran, and if expressed in Hebrew it is the Torah, and this is the statement of Ibn Kullab and those who agreed with him like al-Ash'ari and others. The fourth: that it is eternal letters and sounds combined in pre-eternity, and this is the statement of a group among the people of kalam and hadith. The fifth: that it is letters and sounds, but Allah spoke with them after not having been speaking, and this is the statement of the Karramiyya and others. The sixth: that His speech refers to what His knowledge and will, subsisting in His essence, cause to occur, and this is the statement of the author of al-Mu'tabar, and al-Razi inclines to it in al-Matalib al-Aliya. The seventh: that His speech includes a meaning subsisting in His essence which is what He creates in another, and this is the statement of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. The eighth: that it is shared between the eternal meaning subsisting in the essence and what He creates in another of sounds, and this is the statement of Abu al-Ma'ali and those who followed him. I said: and the apparent is that the first meaning is real (haqiqa) and the second is metaphorical (majaz). The ninth: that He the Exalted does not cease to be speaking when He wills, whenever He wills, and however He wills, and He speaks with a sound that is heard, and the type of speech is eternal even if the specific sound is not eternal. I said: and this supports what we have presented, and it is what is transmitted from the imams of hadith and sunna.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the nine major historical schools of thought on the nature of divine speech (kalam). The commentator lists them in order: (1) The Sabian-philosopher view that speech is an emanation of meanings from the Active Intellect. (2) The Mu'tazilite view that speech is a created entity separate from God. (3) The Kullabi-Ash'ari view that speech is a single eternal meaning in God's essence, expressed in different languages as scripture. (4) The view of some kalam and hadith scholars that speech consists of eternal letters and sounds. (5) The Karramiyya view that God spoke in time after not being speaking, with letters and sounds. (6) The view of the author of al-Mu'tabar and al-Razi that speech reduces to what God's knowledge and will cause. (7) The Maturidi view that speech includes an eternal meaning in God's essence and what He creates in another. (8) Abu al-Ma'ali's view that speech is both the eternal meaning and the created sounds, with the commentator stating that the first meaning is real and the second metaphorical. (9) The view of the Salaf that God is eternally speaking as He wills, with a heard sound, the type eternal but specific sounds temporal; the commentator endorses this view as what is transmitted from the imams. The commentary follows the author's enumeration, explaining each position without evaluation until the end, where he gives his own preference for the ninth view.

Key Terms
الكلام
الصابئة
المتفلسفة
المعتزلة
المعنى الواحد
ابن كلاب
الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Muslims believe divine speech is an eternal attribute.
Correction: In fact, there were early schools like the Mu'tazila who considered it created, and the Sabians considered it an emanation.

Checkpoint
Which view holds that the Quran is a single eternal meaning in God's essence expressed in Arabic?
A) Sabians and philosophers
B) Mu'tazila
C) Ibn Kullab and al-Ash'ari
D) Karramiyya

Key Takeaway
The first three schools offer distinct answers: speech as emanation, as creation, or as eternal meaning—each with different implications for God's attributes and scripture.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Sabians and philosophers reduced divine speech to an intellectual influx. In what ways do you, perhaps unknowingly, treat the Quran as merely a source of abstract ideas rather than as the living, direct word of Allah speaking to you right now? What practical step can you take today to change that?
?
The Mu'tazila believed the Quran was a creation separate from Allah. If you were to fall into a mindset where the Quran feels distant or disconnected from your daily life, what would that say about your belief in its divine origin? How can you actively reassert your conviction that every verse comes directly from Allah?
?
The Ash'aris affirm that the Quran is the expression of a single eternal meaning in Allah's essence. When you recite or hear the Quran, do you sense that you are engaging with something timeless and intimately connected to the very nature of God? If not, what barrier in your heart prevents that awareness, and what will you do to remove it?

Six Further Schools on Divine Speech
Commentator lists the remaining six of nine schools on divine speech, with his own preference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the remaining six positions on divine speech, including the views that speech consists of eternal letters, that God spoke in time, and the preferred Salaf position.

Core Idea
Divine speech: eternal letters, temporal sounds, or a combination?

The commentator continues listing more views, from the claim that speech is eternal letters and sounds to the Karramiyya's temporal speech, and finally to the view he endorses: that God speaks with a sound as He wills. This lesson covers views four through nine, showing the range of positions between eternalism and temporalism.

Guided Path
1
Read the second half of the passage
Read from 'ورابعها' to the end. Notice the numbering continues from the first lesson.
The commentator adds his own remarks after the eighth and ninth views.
2
Identify each view's stance on eternity
For each view, determine whether it considers divine speech eternal or temporal, and whether it involves letters/sounds.
Pay attention to view 9 which distinguishes type (eternal) from specific sound (temporal).
3
Note the commentator's preference
The commentator endorses the ninth view as what is transmitted from the imams. Understand why it might be seen as balanced.

Refutation of Mu'tazila Using the Calf Worshippers
Commentator refutes Mu'tazila by showing the calf worshippers recognized God's speech.

Learning Objective
This lesson establishes that denying God's speech implies a deficiency in divinity, and that even idolaters implicitly recognized speech as a necessary attribute of God, thereby refuting the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Even idolaters knew a true god must speak.

The commentator makes a striking comparison: the golden calf worshippers, despite their idolatry, were more perceptive than the Mu'tazila on the attribute of divine speech. By examining their response to Moses and an anecdote from a famous reciter, this lesson unpack the rational and scriptural proofs that defend the Sunni belief that God speaks in a manner befitting His majesty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the two parts: the rational argument and the anecdote.
2
Understand the comparison
The commentator says the calf worshippers were 'more knowledgeable' than the Mu'tazila. Why? Because they did not deny that God speaks when Moses argued against the calf's divinity.
This shows that speech is inherently tied to divinity in their minds.
3
Examine the anthropomorphism objection
The Mu'tazila object that affirming speech leads to tashbih and tajsim. The commentator's rebuttal is that God's speech is 'as befits His majesty'.
This is the standard Sunni response.
4
Analyze the anecdote
A Mu'tazili asks Abu Amr to change the qira'ah of a verse. Abu Amr's counter-quote from another verse confounds the Mu'tazili. What does this prove?
The anecdote provides irrefutable scriptural evidence that Allah spoke directly to Moses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولعل تكرار هذه المسألة في تأليف الإمام لكمال إهتمام في مقام المرام. ثم علم أن عُبّاد العِجل مع كفرهم بالله أعرف من المعتزلة، لأنه لما قال لهم موسى: ﴿ أَلَمْ يَرَوْا أَنَّهُ لَا يُظْلِمُهُمْ وَلَا يَهْدِيهِمْ سَبِيلًا﴾ [الأعراف: ١٤٨] ، لم يجيبوا بأن ربك لا يتكلم أيضاً ، فعلم أن نفي التكلم نقص يستدل به على عدم ألوهية العجل، وغاية شبهتهم أنهم يقولون: يلزم منه التشبيه والتجسيم، فيقال لهم: إذا قلنا إنه تعالى يتكلم كما يليق بجلاله انتفت شبهتهم. ولقد قال بعضهم لأبي عمرو بن العلاء أحد السبعة من القراء: أريد أن تقرأ وَكَلَّمَ اللهُ مُوسى [النساء :١٦٤]، بنصب اسم الله ليكون موسى هو المتكلم لا الله سبحانه، فقال له أبو عمرو: هب أني قرأت هذه الآية كذا، وكيف تصنع بقوله تعالى: وَلَمَّا جَاءَ مُوسَى لِمِيقَاتِنَا وَكَلَّمَهُ رَبُّهُ [الأعراف: ١٤٣]، فبهت المعتزلي.
Perhaps the repetition of this issue in the composition of the Imam is due to the perfection of his concern in this station. Then know that the worshippers of the calf, despite their disbelief in Allah, are more knowledgeable than the Mu'tazila, because when Moses said to them: 'Did they not see that it does not harm them nor guide them?' [7:148], they did not answer: 'Your Lord does not speak either.' Therefore, it is known that denying speech is a deficiency used to prove the non-divinity of the calf. The utmost of their doubt is that they say: It necessitates anthropomorphism and corporealism. So it is said to them: If we say that He the Exalted speaks as befits His majesty, their doubt is removed. And indeed, one of them said to Abu Amr ibn al-Ala', one of the seven reciters: 'I want you to recite 'And Allah spoke to Moses' [4:164] with the name 'Allah' in the accusative so that Moses would be the speaker, not Allah the Exalted.' So Abu Amr said: 'Suppose I recited this verse like that, what do you do with His saying the Exalted: 'And when Moses came to Our appointed meeting place and his Lord spoke to him' [7:143]?' So the Mu'tazili was confounded.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a polemical argument against the Mu'tazila who deny that God speaks. The commentator first remarks that the Imam (likely Abu Hanifa) repeated this issue due to its importance. He then makes a striking comparison: the worshippers of the golden calf in Moses' time, despite their idolatry, were more perceptive than the Mu'tazila. When Moses argued that the calf did not speak nor guide, they did not respond by denying that God speaks; they implicitly recognized that speech is an essential attribute of divinity. By contrast, the Mu'tazila deny that God speaks, which implies a deficiency in God. Their main objection is that affirming speech leads to anthropomorphism (tashbih) and corporealism (tajsim). The commentator rebuts by stating that God's speech is as befits His majesty, not comparable to human speech. Then he narrates an anecdote: a Mu'tazili asked the renowned Quranic reciter Abu Amr ibn al-Ala' to read the verse 'And Allah spoke to Moses' with the name Allah in the accusative (so that Moses is the subject of 'spoke'), to avoid attributing speech to God. Abu Amr's response was to cite another verse where Allah explicitly says 'and his Lord spoke to him,' which proves that Allah is the one speaking. This confounded the Mu'tazili. The commentator uses both rational argument and scriptural evidence to defend the Sunni position that God speaks in a manner befitting His majesty.

Key Terms
تكلم
عباد العجل
المعتزلة
تشبيه
تجسيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming that God speaks necessarily leads to anthropomorphism (tashbih) or corporealism (tajsim).
Correction: The commentator clarifies that God's speech is 'as befits His majesty' — not comparable to human speech, thus no anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint
How did Abu Amr ibn al-Ala' refute the Mu'tazili who wanted to change the reading of 'وَكَلَّمَ اللهُ مُوسَى'?
A) He refused to change the reading.
B) He cited another verse where Allah directly speaks.
C) He argued that the verse is metaphorical.
D) He agreed with the Mu'tazili.

Key Takeaway
The denial of divine speech is a sign of deficiency in understanding divinity; even idolaters recognized that a true god must speak, and scripture confirms God's speech in a manner befitting His majesty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you allow a philosophical objection to override the clear words of Allah? Reflect on a time when you struggled to accept an attribute of Allah because it seemed 'too human' to you. What will you do differently to affirm Allah's attributes as befits His majesty?
?
The calf worshippers were cognitively dissonant: they recognized a god must speak, yet worshipped a mute idol. In what areas of your life do you claim to believe in the perfection of Allah but then act as if He is silent or indifferent? How can you align your actions with the reality that Allah speaks?
?
The Mu'tazili was confounded by a simple verse. Are there verses of the Qur'an that you have 'reinterpreted' or avoided because they didn't fit your preconceptions? How can you submit your intellect to the Qur'an rather than the other way around?

The Deficiency of Denying God's Speech: Calf-Worshippers and Mu'tazila
The author argues that denying God's speech is a recognized deficiency, using the calf-worshippers and a story with Abu Amr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying God's speech is considered a sign of deficiency, as illustrated by the calf-worshippers' implicit recognition and the rhetorical refutation of a Mu'tazilite objection.

Core Idea
Denying God's speech is a deficiency, as even calf-worshippers recognized.

The author presents a striking comparison: the calf-worshippers, despite their disbelief, were more perceptive than the Mu'tazila on the attribute of speech. By examining the biblical story and a clever exchange with a Quranic reciter, this lesson shows that denying God's speech logically undermines arguments against false deities and leads to absurd conclusions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's argument flow naturally.
Notice the Quranic references in the text.
2
Analyze the calf-worshipper analogy
Understand why the author says calf-worshippers are more knowledgeable than Mu'tazila. When Moses pointed out the calf's inability to harm or guide, they did not deny God's speech.
This shows they recognized lack of speech as a deficiency.
3
Examine the Mu'tazilite objection and response
The Mu'tazila claim that affirming speech leads to anthropomorphism. The author responds that God speaks in a manner befitting His majesty, which removes the objection.
This is the core theological refutation.
4
Reflect on the Abu Amr anecdote
See how a Mu'tazilite wanted to change the grammar of a verse to make Moses the speaker. Abu Amr's counter-quote from another verse left the Mu'tazilite confounded.
This shows the futility of denying God's speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم علم أن عُبّاد العِجل مع كفرهم بالله أعرف من المعتزلة، لأنه لما قال لهم موسى: ﴿ أَلَمْ يَرَوْا أَنَّهُ لَا يُظْلِمُهُمْ وَلَا يَهْدِيهِمْ سَبِيلًا﴾ [الأعراف: ١٤٨]، لم يجيبوا بأن ربك لا يتكلم أيضاً ، فعلم أن نفي التكلم نقص يستدل به على عدم ألوهية العجل، وغاية شبهتهم أنهم يقولون: يلزم منه التشبيه والتجسيم، فيقال لهم: إذا قلنا إنه تعالى يتكلم كما يليق بجلاله انتفت شبهتهم. ولقد قال بعضهم لأبي عمرو بن العلاء أحد السبعة من القراء: أريد أن تقرأ وَكَلَّمَ اللهُ مُوسى [النساء :١٦٤]، بنصب اسم الله ليكون موسى هو المتكلم لا الله سبحانه، فقال له أبو عمرو: هب أني قرأت هذه الآية كذا، وكيف تصنع بقوله تعالى: وَلَمَّا جَاءَ مُوسَى لِمِيْقَاتِنَا وَ كَلَّمَهُ رَابُّهُ الاعراف : ١٤٣]، فبهت المعتزلي.
Then know that the worshippers of the calf, despite their disbelief in God, are more knowledgeable than the Muʿtazila. For when Moses said to them, 'Do they not see that it does not harm them nor guide them to a way?' (al-Aʿrāf 7:148), they did not reply, 'Your Lord does not speak either.' So it is known that denying speech is a deficiency used to argue against the divinity of the calf. The utmost of their (the Muʿtazila's) suspicion is that they say: it necessitates anthropomorphism and corporealism. So it is said to them: if we say that He, exalted, speaks in a manner befitting His majesty, their suspicion is removed. And one of them said to Abu ʿAmr ibn al-ʿAlāʾ, one of the seven reciters: 'I want you to recite "and Allah spoke to Moses" (al-Nisāʾ 4:164) with the name of Allah in the accusative so that Moses would be the speaker, not Allah.' So Abu ʿAmr said: 'Suppose I recite this verse like that, what will you do with His statement: "And when Moses came to Our appointed time and His Lord spoke to him" (al-Aʿrāf 7:143)?' So the Muʿtazilite was confounded.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Muʿtazilite denial that God speaks. The author begins by making a striking comparison: the Israelites who worshipped the calf were more perceptive than the Muʿtazila. When Moses rebuked them, pointing out that the calf could neither harm nor guide them, they did not respond by denying that God speaks. They recognized that lack of speech is a deficiency, which is why Moses used it to argue against the calf's divinity. The Muʿtazila, however, claim that affirming speech for God leads to anthropomorphism (tashbīh) and corporealism (tajsīm). The author answers that if we affirm God speaks in a manner befitting His majesty, the suspicion vanishes. He then narrates an incident: a Muʿtazilite asked the famous qārīʾ Abu ʿAmr ibn al-ʿAlāʾ to read the verse 'wa-kallama Allahu Mūsā' (and Allah spoke to Moses) with the accusative (Allaha) so that Moses becomes the speaker. Abu ʿAmr cleverly countered by asking how then he would explain the verse 'wa-lammā jāʾa Mūsā li-mīqātinā wa-kallamahu rabbuhu' (and when Moses came to Our appointed time and his Lord spoke to him), where clearly God is the speaker. The Muʿtazilite was left speechless.

Key Terms
نفي التكلم
المعتزلة
عبّاد العجل
أبو عمرو بن العلاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming that God speaks necessarily leads to anthropomorphism (tashbīh) and corporealism (tajsīm).
Correction: God speaks in a manner that befits His majesty, without resembling creation, thus removing the supposed contradiction.

Checkpoint
What was the Muʿtazilite's request to Abu ʿAmr?
A) To read a verse with a different qirāʾa
B) To change the grammatical case to make Moses the speaker
C) To deny the verse
D) To affirm anthropomorphism

Key Takeaway
Denying God's speech is a sign of deficiency, as even the calf-worshippers implicitly recognized, and the Mu'tazilite attempt to avoid it through grammatical manipulation fails against the clear Quranic text.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The calf-worshippers recognized that a silent idol could not be divine. Have you ever considered the 'silence' in your own life—areas where you avoid acknowledging God's speech because it demands something of you? What excuse do you use, similar to the Mu'tazilite's fear of anthropomorphism, to avoid submitting to God's clear words?
?
Abu Amr confounded the Mu'tazilite with a single verse. Is there a verse of the Quran that you have been avoiding because it contradicts your desires? What would it mean for you to accept that God truly speaks through His book, even when it makes you uncomfortable?
?
The author says that denying God's speech is a deficiency. In what ways might you be 'denying God's speech' in your daily life—ignoring the Quran's commands, downplaying its warnings, or rationalizing away its clear injunctions? What step will you take today to remedy that?
